Jamison Brereton

97 (809)
Soma Pavama╠Дna
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi 1тАУ3, Indrapramati V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 4тАУ6, Vrс╣г╠е agaс╣Зa V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 7тАУ9, Manyu V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 10тАУ12, Upamanyu V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 13тАУ15, Vy─Бghrap─Бd V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 16тАУ18, ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 19тАУ21, Karс╣Зa┼Ыrut V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 22тАУ24, Mrс╕╖╠е─лka V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 25тАУ27, Vasukra V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha 28тАУ30, Par─Б┼Ыara ┼Ъ─Бktya 31тАУ44, Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa 45тАУ58
58 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, arranged in trcas ╠е
This is the longest hymn in the R╠еgveda, consisting of fifty-eight verses, arranged in three-verse units. It is also the last IXth Maс╣Зс╕Нala hymn in triс╣гс╣нubh. Despite its extraordinary length, it can be analyzed as consisting of a series of originally independent tr╠еcas combined into one, and it therefore conforms to the prevailing principles of arrangement in the Saс╣Гhit─Б. In the first half (vss. 1тАУ30) each tr╠еca is attributed to Vasiс╣гс╣нha or to a different Vasiс╣гс╣нhid; the second half is divided between two, non-Vasiс╣гс╣нhid, poets. If we assume that the tr╠еca division continues in this sec
ond half (as most scholars do), the Anukramaс╣З─л ascription does not conform to the tr╠еca division, as the first two verses of the tr╠еca of verses 43тАУ45 are credited to Par─Б┼Ыara ┼Ъ─Бktya and the last one to Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa. There is also an extra verse, most probably the final one (58), which contains the Kutsa refrain of Maс╣Зс╕Нala I (I.94.16cd, etc.). Although according to the Anukramaс╣З─л each of these poets is responsible for fourteen verses, there is no more apparent unity in these larger stretches than in the individual tr╠еcas of the first half.
As is often the case in such long, composite hymns, the tr╠еcas exhibit varying degrees of cohesiveness, from the tight and emphatic verbal repetitions of verses 49тАУ51 to the diffuseness of groupings like verses 7тАУ9, 40тАУ42. Some of the tr╠еcas, though not thematically or verbally unified, have a third verse that marks it as final; for instance, the first two tr╠еcas (vss. 1тАУ3, 4тАУ6) each end with the Vasiс╣гс╣нha clan refrain as the last p─Бda, and the final verse of three tr╠еcas begins with a summary ev─Б╠Б тАЬthusтАЭ (vss. 13тАУ15, 19тАУ21, 25тАУ27), a word characteristic of final verses.
As might be expected, the contents of this hymn are also extremely various, but generally exhibit the standard tropes of soma hymns: the mechanisms of

soma preparation, including the journey across the filter and the mixing with waters and with milk; the power of soma to incite the gods, especially Indra, and the power of the ritualists and, especially, the poets, to strengthen the soma for this task; and the rewards the ritualists will receive from properly prepar
ing the soma. Nonetheless, the hymn contains a number of striking similes and metaphors, and some passages of great difficulty, chief among which is the tr╠еca of verses 52тАУ54, which may (or may not) be a d─Бnastuti and whose translation here is provisional in places. Note also verse 38, which in our interpretation con
tains an archaic formula denoting an archaic figure, the тАЬPlacer of the SunтАЭ (see Jamison 2010).

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the structure of this, the longest hymn in the RV, see published introduction. It consists of tс╣Ыcas with varying degrees of cohesion.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe shining Somabeing purified by the golden hand that urges it forth, brings its juice into contact with the gods; when effused it proceeds with a roar to the filter like the ministrant priest to the halls prepared (for sacrifice) containing victims.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Being purified by his impulsion, his drive, the god has intermingled his sap with the gods.
Pressed, he goes rasping around the filter like the Hotar around the fixed seats provided with (sacrificial) animals.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Renou points out, init. asy├б is reflexive or pseudo-reflexive, referring to Soma.

Grassmann attributes the instr. preс╣г─Б╠Бto a root noun pr├йс╣г- (тЖР pra-├нс╣г-). Scarlatta (59-60) discusses the form extensively, pointing out that a root noun analysis is dispreferred because of the accent on the ending: root nouns generally keeping the accent on the root even in the oblique. An instr. to a putative them. stem preс╣г├б- is possible (at least accentually distinct from pr├йс╣гa- I.68.5).

Almost identical to IX.92.6a, p─Бda d contains one of the few technical references to animal sacrifice (other than the horse sacrifice) in the RV.

He goes, effused and singing, to the filter, like priest to measured seats supplied with cattle.

English translation:

тАЬ(Soma), the most famous of the famous, the earht-born, the conciliator, is cleansed for us in the elevated fleece; sound aloud in the firmament when purified; do you ever protect us with blessings.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sound aloud: dhanv─Б = imperative of dhanv

Jamison Brereton

The dear one is groomed on the sheepтАЩs back, the more glorious of the glorious ones, a fellow countryman at our side.
Cry out, run, as you are being purified. тАУ Do you protect us always with your blessings.

p┼лс╣г├йva dh─лj├бvano тАШsi soma, which is, of course, a good arg. Dear, he is brightened on the fleecy summit, a Prince among us, nobler than the noble.
Roar out as thou art purified, run forward. Do ye preserve us evermore with blessings.

English translation:

тАЬSing (to the Soma), let us praise the gods; send forth the Soma for (the acquisition of) great wealth. He passes sweet-flavoured pure through the fleecy filter; our (Soma) devoted to the gods alights on the pitcher.тАЭ

Sing forth: let us recite to the gods. Impel Soma for great stakes.
The sweet one will purify himself across the sheepтАЩs fleece. He will sit in the tub, seeking the gods for us. с│У

Griffith

Let us sing praises to the Gods: sing loudly, send ye the Soma forth for mighty riches.
Let him flow, sweetly-flavoured, through the filter, and let our pious one rest in the pitcher.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndu coming to obtain the friendship of the god; flows in a thousand streams for (their) exhilaration, glorified by the priests (he proceeds) to his ancient station, he proceeds to Indra for the sake of great prosperity (to the worshippers).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The drop, coming here to fellowship with the gods, purifies himself in a thousand streams for exhilaration.
Being praised by men, he has gone along his earlier domain, to Indra for great good portion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner and Renou take ├бnu dh─Б╠Бma p┼л╠Бrvam as referring to an earlier mode of praise (e.g., тАЬnach der fr├╝heren WeiseтАЭ), but dh─Б╠Бman- in soma hymns tends, in my view, to refer to the physical domain(s) of the ritual ground, which Soma typically travels across in the course of his ritual preparation. See, e.g., the exx. in the immediately preceding hymn IX.96.18-19 and comm. thereon).

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Renou points out (ad vs. 6), the key to this tс╣Ыca is the dative of purpose: 4b dh├бn─Бya, 5b m├бd─Бya, 5d mahat├й sa├║bhag─Бya, 6b bh├бr─Бya.

Griffith

Winning the friendship of the Deities, Indu flows in a thousand streams to make them joyful.
Praised by the men after the ancient statute, he hath come nigh, for our great bliss, to Indra.

Geldner

English translation:

тАЬ(Soma), when our praise is offered, flow green-tinted and purified, to (bring us) riches, may your exhilarating beverage animate Indra to battle. Go in the same car with the gods to (procure us) wealth; do you ever protect us with blessings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As a fallow bay, rush for wealth for the praiser as you are being purified. Let your exhilarating drink go to Indra for the taking.
Drive on the same chariot with the gods to bounty. тАУ Do you protect us always with your blessings.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬReciting sacred praise like Uс╣гanas the praiser (Vс╣Ыс╣гagaс╣Зa) proclaims the births of the gods; assiduous in pious observances, of brilliant radiance, purifying (from sin), he approaches the filter making a noise (as) a wild boar (makes a noise) with its foot.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The praiser: devaс╕е = Soma; as a wild boar makes a noise with its foot: var─Бhaс╕е = effused on a good (vara) day (ahan)– epithet of Soma;

Pada = pad─Бni, abodes, i.e., the filters

Jamison Brereton

Speaking forth his poetry like U┼Ыan─Б, the god proclaims the races of the gods.
Of great commandment, of blazing lineage, pure, as a boar he goes
rasping toward his tracks.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the expression k─Б╠Бvyam u┼Ы├бneva the first word is the acc. obj. of bruv─Бс╣З├бс╕е, but it is also of course a play on the patrynomic of U┼Ыan─Б, the differently accented k─Бvy├б-.

In d the published translation takes pad─Б╠Бas neut. pl., based on IX.12.8 abh├н priy─Б╠Бdiv├бs pad─Б╠Б, тАж arс╣гati тАЬSoma rushes towards the dear tracks of heaven,тАЭ adduced by Renou

However, it is also possible and, I now think, desirable to interpr. it as an instr. sg.

тАЬalong the track.тАЭ I would not interpr. the instr., with Geldner, as тАЬmit dem Fusse.тАЭ On PREV eti r├йbhan# see IX.96.6=17, IX.97.1 (this hymn) and with emi VII.18.22; тАЬsnortingтАЭ or тАЬgruntingтАЭ would be a better rendering of r├йbhan in the boar context.

The God declares the Deities’ generations, like Usana, proclaiming lofty wisdom.
With brilliant kin, far-ruling, sanctifying, the Boar advances, singing, to the places.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣рдВрд╕рд╛рд╕рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рд░реНрд╣рдиреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рд╣рдВрд╕рд╛рдЗрд╡ рдЪрд░рдиреНрддреЛрд╡рд╛рд╡реГрд╖рдЧрдгрд╛рдГ рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХрд╛рдЛрд╖рдпрдГ рдЕрдорд╛рддреН рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдмрд▓рд╛рддреН рддреНрд░рд╛рд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдГрд╕рдиреНрддрдГ рддреГрдкрд▓рдВ рддреНрдЛрдкрд▓рд╢рдмреНрджрдГрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдЪрд╛рд░реА рддрджреБрдХреНрддрдВрдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХреЗрдитАФрддреГрдкрд▓рдкреНрд░рднрд░реНрдорд╛- рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдкреНрд░рд╣рд╛рд░реАрддрд┐ ред рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдкреНрд░рд╣рд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдореНрдордиреНрдпреБрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдирднрд┐рд╣рдиреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рд╕реЛрдордВ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ рдЕрднрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рдЕрд╕реНрддрдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реБрдГ рдкреНрд░рдпрд╛рд╕рд┐рд╖реБрдГ рдкреНрд░рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрддрдГ рд╕рдЦрд╛рдпрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддреНрдпрд╕реНрддреЛрддреГрддреНрд╡рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгреЗрди рд╕рдореНрдмрдиреНрдзреЗрди рд╕рдЦрд┐рднреВрддрд╛рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддрд╛рд░рдГ рдЖрдЩреНрдЧреВрд╖реНрдпрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реИрд░рднрд┐рдЧрдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдШреЛрд╖рд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рдкреГрд╖реЛрджрд░рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд╛рдЩреНрдЧреВрд╖рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреЗрд╢рдГ рдЖрдЩреН рдЕрдиреБрдирд╛рд╕рд┐рдХрд╢реНрдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдГ рд╕реНрддреЛрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрд╣рдВ рджреБрд░реНрдорд░реНрд╖рдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрднрд┐рд░реНрджреБрд░реНрдзрд░рдВ рджреБрдГрд╕рд╣рдВ рдПрд╡рдВрд╡рд┐рдзрдВрд╕реЛрдордВ рдкрд╡рдорд╛рдирдореБрджреНрджрд┐рд╢реНрдп рд╡рд╛рдгрдВ рд╡рд╛рджреНрдпрд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдВ рд╕рд╛рдХрдВ рд╕рд╣реИрд╡рдкреНрд░рд╡рджрдиреНрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╛рджрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреБрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддрдВ рдЧрд╛рдирдЩреНрдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее рео рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Vс╣Ыс╣гagaс╣Зas (walking like) swans, (alarmed) at the strength (of the foe), having repaired to the house of sacrifice, to the swift-shooting foe-despising (Soma), the friends sound the flut to the praiseworthy irresistble Pavam─Бna.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Walking like swans: haс╣Гs─Бsaс╕е = wounded by the enemy;

Am─Бt = ┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm bal─Бt tr─Бsit─Бс╕е santaс╕е; another interpretation: the vс╣Ыс╣гagaс╣Зas have gone from hence to their home

Jamison Brereton

The geese have journeyed forth to (SomaтАЩs) sharp battle-fury, from nearby to their home, in a bullish flock.
The comrades speak in unison to the self-purifying one a songful music difficult to forget.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of this vs. differs from the standard because I donтАЩt interpr.

anything here as a PN, unlike Geldner and to a lesser extent Renou In particular, tс╣Ыp├бlamany├║- is taken as PN by Grassmann, Geldner, Renou, Mayr (PN); Geldner and (waveringly) both Oldenberg and Mayr (PN) also so interpr. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гagaс╣Зa-. As for the former, tс╣Ыp├бla- is also found in the cmpd. tс╣Ыp├бla-prabharman- (X.89.5, where it is adjacent to ─Б╠Бp─Бnta-manyu-, with - manyu- as here), both adj. applying to Soma. There is no question of a PN there. It is also likely to be related to tс╣Ыpr├б- (VIII.2.5), also of Soma. See comm. ad loc., where I accept MayrтАЩs (EWA s.v.) suggestion that tс╣Ыpr├б- means тАШsharpтАЩ. The other part of the dyad, many├║-, is of course a well-attested common noun тАШbattle furyтАЩ. I see no obstacle to interpr. the phrase as тАЬsharp battle fury,тАЭ referring to SomaтАЩs martial progress across the ritual ground.

In the standard tr. the geese of p─Бda a are in an unmarked simile, and the real subj. is vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гagaс╣З─Бс╕е, which is either a PN (Geldner) or a descriptor of officiants (Renou: тАЬLes (officiants formant) un groupe m├вleтАЭ). But again, nothing stands in the way of taking the geese as the subj., modified by vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гagaс╣З─Бс╕е; after all, geese come in flocks! In my view the geese are, metaphorically, the singers (so not too far from Renou), who attend the ritual in a flock. The point of comparison is the noise they make; cf., e.g., IX.32.3 ─Б╠Бd ─лс╣Г haс╣Гs├│ y├бth─Б gaс╣З├бm, v├н┼Ыvasy─Бv─лva┼Ыan m├бtim тАЬjust as (the lead) wild goose (sets) its flock (to honking), he has made the thought of everyone bellow.тАЭ The last two vss. here (7-8) contrast the harsh noise made by Soma (compared to a boar, 7d) with the equally harsh noise of honking geese, representing the ritual singers. This may be far from the mellifluous singing we imagine, but, as I have long argued, the root тИЪribh тАШrasp,тАЩ etc. and its deriv. noun rebh├б- do not flatter the sound of the singers: they describe the squawking of birds of prey and the creaking of a wagon, inter alia (see comm. ad VI.3.6, IX.66.9). Although the principal image here is of noisily honking geese, the migratory travels of the geese (going from nearby us to their [winter?] home) provide a secondary image. Because in real life the honking of geese is generally perceived as they cross the sky in formation, the two images go together.

Geldner and Renou take c with ab, with p├бvam─Бnam another goal (beside Tс╣Ыpala Manyu) of ay─Бsuс╕е. I take it rather with d, and I think the 2nd hemistich softens and repairs the uncompromising tunelessness of the noise in ab, by revising the depiction of the singers. They are now тАЬcomrades,тАЭ and they speak forth (pra тИЪvad, with double acc.) to Soma тАЬsongful musicтАЭ (─Бс╣Еguс╣гy├аm тАж v─Бс╣З├бm). Geldner and Renou take ─Бс╣Еguс╣гy├аm as modifying p├бvam─Бnam, and in their favor the two words are adjacent.

But the only other occurrence of that stem modifies s─Б╠Бman- тАШmelodyтАЩ (I.62.2) and to bleach it to тАШpreislichenтАЩ (for which there are already numerous other synonyms) seems unfortunate. I would suggest that the prominent initial position of ─Бс╣Еguс╣гy├аm in c, far from its head noun at the end of d, results from this intention to re-cast the harsh image of ab and do so as soon as possible.

English translation:

тАЬHe moves rapidly (following) the path of (him) the much-praised, (other) goers cannot overtake him (though he is) moving easily; sharp-horned he displays manifold (radiance); the Soma appears green-tinted by day, and clearly visible at night.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Soma appears green-tinted by day: Soma is not visible in the daylight;

с╣Ъjra = straight going, с╣Ыju-g─Бm─л, i.e., clearly visible, vispaс╣гс╣нaс╕е = red or brown

Jamison Brereton

He hastens at the pace of the wide-ranging one [=Viс╣гс╣Зu?]. The cows, as they seem to bellow, give their measure to the one who plays at will
[=Soma].
The sharp-horned one makes himself an ample (face). By day he
appears tawny, but silvery by night.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. presents a number of puzzles, esp. in p─Бda b.

The verb in p─Бda a, raс╣Гhate, should be intransitive. I construe the acc. j┼лt├нm loosely, as indicating the pace or speed at which Soma moves, which is compared to that of Viс╣гс╣Зu, who is regularly modified by urug─Бy├б-, though the adj. is not exclusive to him.

The phrase vс╣Ы╠Бth─Б kr─лс╕╖├бnt- is also found in IX.21.3. ItтАЩs also worth noting that vс╣Ы╠Бth─Б is also found with several instances of p─Б╠Бjas- тАШface, dimensionтАЩ disc. below (IX.76.1=88.5, 109.21).

The problems in p─Бda b center on the root affiliation of the verb mimate and the function of n├б. The phrase in question is mimate n├б g─Б╠Бvaс╕е. The p─Бda is incisively and persuasively discussed by Oldenberg, with whose analysis my own is in general agreement. To begin with n├б, both Geldner and Renou take it as neg., but as Oldenberg points out, its position is against that. I think that it is the simile marker, but, unusually, marking the verb that precedes it as to be read in two senses, rather than marking a nominal phrase as the simile, as is its overwhelming use.

This brings us to the verb. Given the presence of cows, our first impulse is to think тАШbellowтАЩ; cf., e.g., IX.33.4 g─Б╠Бvo mimanti dhen├бvaс╕е. But, though тИЪm─Б тАШbellowтАЩ does have the requisite redupl. pres. stem m├нm─Б-/ m├нm-, it is only active, as Oldenberg also points out. I therefore think that n├б here signals that mimate is an imperfect pun: it gestures towards тАШbellowтАЩ, but cannot belong to тАШbellowтАЩ because of the middle voice. (Oldenberg also thinks the pun is present.) This accounts for my тАЬas they seem to bellowтАЭ in the published translation The root to which the verb actually belongs is тИЪm─Б тАШmeasureтАЩ, which also has a redupl. pres., which, however, is generally middle. The voice of the verb in our passage thus favors тИЪm─Б тАШmeasureтАЩ, though тИЪm─Б тАШbellowтАЩ, at least initially, seems to fit the context better. What can тАШmeasureтАЩ contribute? This question was ingeniously answered by Oldenberg: the cows, i.e., the milk mixture, тАЬteilen ihm das Mass zu.тАЭ They тАЬgive him their measure,тАЭ that is, provide him further physical substance as he travels through the stages of his ritual preparation.

This image is continued in c, by the VP par─лс╣Зas├бс╣Г kс╣Ыс╣Зute. Although the acc. is generally taken as a substantivized neut. to a them. adj. par─лс╣Зas├б- derived from the noun p├бr─лс╣Зas- тАШfullness, profusionтАЩ (so Grassmann; see AiG II.2.137), I consider it still an adj., with which we should supply p─Б╠Бjas- тАШface, dimensionтАЩ. This has good support in IX; cf. IX.76.1 = IX.88.5 vс╣Ы╠Бth─Б p─Б╠Бj─Бс╣Гsi kr╠ес╣Зute тАЬhe deploys his full dimensions at willтАЭ and with a different medial verb IX.68.3 p─Б╠Бja ─Б╠Бdade тАЬhe assumed his full dimensionтАЭ (see also IX.109.21). The added milk allows him to expand and attain ample size or measure. On the association of cows/milk with par─лс╣Зas(a)- see VIII.45.24 g├│-par─лс╣Зasa-, characterizing soma drinks. In the comm. ad VIII.45.24 I suggest that the 2nd cmpd member is par─лс╣Зas├б- as here (hence a 2nd occurrence of that stem), not p├бr─лс╣Зas- (per Grassmann, etc.).

Acdg. to Geldner (n. 9cd), Renou, L├╝ders (267), p─Бda d depicts Soma as sun and moon.

This may well be, but I wonder if the source of the contrastive image is not the Overnight (atir─Бtr├б) soma ritual.

English translation:

тАЬThe powerful, flowing Soma having quantities o fjuice flowing down, streams forth infusing strength into Indra for his exhilaration; conferring wealth the king of strength slays the r─Бkс╣гasas and harasses the enemy.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The prizewinning drop purifies himself, bringing cows down in floodтАФ Soma stimulating the power in Indra, for exhilaration.
He smashes demonic force; he deflects hostilities, making wide space as king of the community.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The sense and derivation of g├│-nyoghas- are disputed. Geldner tr. тАЬder die K├╝he w├╝rdigtтАЭ and tentatively connects the 2nd member with what he cites as ny ├▓hate in V.52.11. I do not construe n├н with ohate in that passage (see comm. ad loc.), in part because тИЪuh does not otherwise appear with n├н. The sense he attributes to the cmpd is also rather jarring. He is followed in both sense (тАЬrespectant les vachesтАЭ) and derivation by Renou, who adds to the dossier of parallels I.180.5 g├│r ├│heс╣Зa, which, however, is too riddled with uncertainties (see comm. ad loc.) to provide good evidence. By contrast Oldenberg considers BRтАЩs conjectured emendation *g├│-nyokas- тАШaccustomed to cowsтАЩ (?тАФhe doesnтАЩt gloss) very likely. He rejects the view that the cmpd as transmitted contains an s-stem oghas- тАШfloodтАЩ, related to later Vedic ogha-, augh├б- тАШfloodтАЩ (even though he states that if we stick with the transmitted text he would tr. тАЬauf den die Kuh(milch) hernieder flutetтАЭ). This dismissal of a potential

*oghas- is shared by Mayr (EWA s.v. ogha-): тАЬRV 9,97,10 g├│nyoghas- ist nicht f├╝r ein ved. *oghas- тАШStr├╢mungтАЩ verwertbar.тАЭ Mayr instead tentatively follows the Geldner/Renou interpr. (s.v. OH), тАЬvielleicht тАШdie K├╝he preisendтАЩ od. dgl.тАЭ I am puzzled by this blanket rejection, esp. from Mayr, who cites (s.v. ogha-) with approbation NartenтАЩs positing (YH 221) of an Indo-Iranian root тИЪ*uag╠п h тАШfliessenтАЩ, found in ogha-, augh├б-.

Admittedly, there is no independently attested s-stem *├│ghas-. But consider the semantically and morphologically parallel g├│-arс╣Зas- (4x) тАШhaving a flood of cowsтАЩ, with the well-attested s-stem ├бrс╣Зas- тАШfloodтАЩ. It is easy (at least for me) to imagine that an s-stem *├│ghas- was coined in analogy to ├бrс╣Зas- for just this cmpd.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca is attributed to Manyu V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, with the name possibly extracted from the previous tс╣Ыca, where many├║- in 8a is taken by some as part of a PN (see comm. above).

All three vss. contain a hemistich beginning ├нnduс╕е (10a, 11c, 12c); the verb pavate appears in all three (10a, 11b, 12a), though this is hardly unusual. In addition there is the presence of Indra (10b, 11c) or the gods in general (12b), as well as shared vocabulary: hemistich-final m├бd─Бya (10b, 11d), тИЪpс╣Ыc тАШinfuseтАЩ (11a, 12b), #dev├│ dev├бsya (11d) / #dev├│ dev─Б╠Бn (12d). The net result is an impression of unity, despite the lack of a striking shared theme and the unremarkable nature of the shared material.

Griffith

Strong Indu, bathed in milk, flows on for Indra, Soma exciting strength, to make him joyful.
He quells malignities and slays the demons, the King of mighty power who brings us comfort.

Geldner

Der Saft, der Preisrenner, der die K├╝he w├╝rdigt, l├дutert sich, der Soma, der in Indra die Kraft weckt, zum Rausche. Er schl├дgt den b├╢sen Geist, h├дlt die Unholdinnen ab, einen Ausweg schaffend, der K├╢nig des Opferbundes.

Grassmann

Der schnelle Indu str├╢mt zu K├╝hen eilend, dem Indra Kraft zum Rausch erregend, Soma, Er schl├дgt Gespenster, st├╢sst hinweg die B├╢sen, des Stammes K├╢nig weiten Segen schaffend.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдзрд╛рдерд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдЕрджреНрд░рд┐рджреБрдЧреНрдзрд╛рдГ рдЧреНрд░рд╛рд╡рднрд┐рд░реНрджреЗрдЙрдЧреНрдзреЛрднрд┐рд╖реБрддрдГ рд╕реЛрдордГ рдордзреНрд╡рд╛ рдорджрдХрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреНрдпрд╛рдзрд╛рд░рдпрд╛ рдкреГ- рдЪрд╛рдирдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╕рдореНрдкрд░реНрдЪрдпрдиреН рд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЬрдпрдиреН рд░реЛрдо рдЕрд╡рд┐рд░реЛрдорднрд┐рдГ рдХреГрддрдВ рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░рдВ рддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрдХреГрддреНрдп рд╡реНрдпрд╡рдзрд╛- рдпрдХрдЩреНрдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдкрд╡рддреЗ рдХрд▓рд╢реЗрд╖реБ рдХреНрд╖рд░рддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╕рдЦреНрдпрдВ рд╕рдЦрд┐рднрд╛рд╡рдЩреНрдХрд░реНрдорд╡рд╛ рдЬреБрд╖рд╛рдгрдГ рд╕реЗрд╡рдорд╛рдирдГ рджреЗрд╡реЛрджреНрдпреЛрддрдорд╛рдирдГ рдорддреНрд╕рд░реЛрдорджрдХрд░рдЗрдиреНрджреБрдГ рд╕реЛрдордГ рджреЗрд╡рд╕реНрдпреЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рдорджрд╛рдп рдорджрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдкрд╡рддреЗ рдХреНрд╖рд░рддрд┐ рее резрез рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMilked forth by the stones the Soma flows through the (sheep’s) hair coming into contact (with the gods) with its sweet-flavoured stream; the divine exhilarating Indu desiring the friendship of Indra flows for the exhilaration of the deity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Then being infused with honey in a stream, he purifies himself across the fleece, when he has been milked by the stone,
the drop enjoying the fellowship of Indra, the god, the exhilarating
drink of the god, for exhilaration.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The 2nd hemistich contains three pairs of phonological and (partly) etymological figures: #├нndur ├нndrasya, #dev├│ dev├бsya, matsar├│ m├бd─Бya#, with the 1st two presenting matching nom.+gen. grammatical figures.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca is attributed to Manyu V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, with the name possibly extracted from the previous tс╣Ыca, where many├║- in 8a is taken by some as part of a PN (see comm. above).

All three vss. contain a hemistich beginning ├нnduс╕е (10a, 11c, 12c); the verb pavate appears in all three (10a, 11b, 12a), though this is hardly unusual. In addition there is the presence of Indra (10b, 11c) or the gods in general (12b), as well as shared vocabulary: hemistich-final m├бd─Бya (10b, 11d), тИЪpс╣Ыc тАШinfuseтАЩ (11a, 12b), #dev├│ dev├бsya (11d) / #dev├│ dev─Б╠Бn (12d). The net result is an impression of unity, despite the lack of a striking shared theme and the unremarkable nature of the shared material.

English translation:

тАЬClothed in plural asant radiance suited to the season, the sportive Indu flows purified, reaching the gods with its juice; the ten fingers guide it to the elevated fleece.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He purifies himself toward his own dear (tracks?), while being purified, the god infusing the gods with his own sap.
The drop, clothing himself in his foundations according to the ritual order, has enwrapped himself in the ten fingers on the back of the sheep.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first p─Бda is alliterative: тАж priy─Б╠Бс╣Зi pavate pun─Бn├бс╕е, while opening of the 2nd is an etymological figure that matches the one opening 11d.

The referent of priy─Б╠Бс╣Зi, the obj. or goal of abh├н тАж pavate, is uncertain. In the pub. tr. I supply тАШtracksтАЩ, on the basis of 7c pad─Б╠БтАж abhy ├иti, as well as IX.12.8 abh├н priy─Б╠Бdiv├бs pad─Б╠БтАж arс╣гati тАЬhe rushes towards the dear tracks of heaven.тАЭ However, as noted above, I no longer think pad─Б╠Бin vs. 7 is an acc. pl., and I am also more moved by GeldnerтАЩs cited parallel, IX.75.1 abh├н priy─Б╠Бс╣Зi pavate …, n─Б╠Бm─Бni тАЬhe purifies himself towards his own dear names.тАЭ But cf. also IX.57.2 abh├н priy─Б╠Бс╣Зi k─Б╠Бvy─Б …

arс╣гati. I would now be inclined to supply тАШnamesтАЩ (тАЬhe purifies himself towards his own dear namesтАЭ), since SomaтАЩs progress across the ritual ground to his names is a trope (see comm. ad IX.75.1). But since there are a number of other referential possibilities for the construction abh├н priy─Б╠Б(с╣Зi), it might be best simply to tr.

тАЬtowards his own dear (things).тАЭ P─Бda c is also puzzling: the phrase тАЬclothing himself in his foundationsтАЭ (dh├бrm─Бс╣Зi тАж v├бs─Бnaс╕е) is not immediately interpretable, and there are no illuminating parallels (at least that I have found). The adverbial с╣Ыtuth─Б╠БтАЬaccording to the ritual orderтАЭ suggests that the process of тАЬclothing himselfтАЭ involves following the orderly steps of the sacrifice - which in turn suggests that Soma is making his progress across the ritual ground, encountering first the waters, then the milk, before arriving at his destination. I therefore think that the тАЬfoundationsтАЭ here are the waters and the milk - his supports, the materials of which the soma drink is built. But this cannot be demonstrated.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca is attributed to Manyu V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, with the name possibly extracted from the previous tс╣Ыca, where many├║- in 8a is taken by some as part of a PN (see comm. above).

All three vss. contain a hemistich beginning ├нnduс╕е (10a, 11c, 12c); the verb pavate appears in all three (10a, 11b, 12a), though this is hardly unusual. In addition there is the presence of Indra (10b, 11c) or the gods in general (12b), as well as shared vocabulary: hemistich-final m├бd─Бya (10b, 11d), тИЪpс╣Ыc тАШinfuseтАЩ (11a, 12b), #dev├│ dev├бsya (11d) / #dev├│ dev─Б╠Бn (12d). The net result is an impression of unity, despite the lack of a striking shared theme and the unremarkable nature of the shared material.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Calling out for the praises like) a red bull bellowing after the kine; the Soma goes with a roar through heaven and earth; (his voice) is heard as the voice of Indra, manifesting (himself) he raises this voice.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The ruddy bull keeps roaring at the cows; bellowing he goes to heaven and earth.
His voice, like IndraтАЩs, is heard at the contest. He rushes, making this speech perceptible here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The part. nad├бyan here (as well as the other 2 forms of this stem) is universally taken as a trans.-caus. тАШcausing to resoundтАЩ with Heaven and Earth as obj.

As I argue in my -├бya-book (60-61), all 3 passages are better taken as intrans. In this vs. the focus is on the noise that Soma makes; see esp. the parallel part.

abhik├бnikradat тАШconstantly roaringтАЩ. And so intrans. тАШbellowingтАЩ fits this pattern.

Note also IX.70.6 m─Бt├бr─Б тАж n─Б╠Бnadad eti тАЬhe goes bellowing to his two mothers [=Heaven and Earth,тАЭ with the same config. of participle to тИЪnad + eti + H+E.

13-15 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

No particular signs of cohesion in this tс╣Ыca, which is a collection of soma tropes. If there is any unifying theme it is movement, with eti (13b), eс╣гi (14b, c), arс╣гati (13d), arс╣гa (15d); for other repeated lexical items also pariс╣гicy├бm─Бnaс╕е (14d), p├бri тАж sikt├бс╕е (15d). Also the final vs. (15) begins with ev─Б╠Б, the common hymn-ending summary particle - an effect that is muted in the published translation

The poet is supposed to be Upamanyu V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, presumably following up on the Manyu to whom the last tс╣Ыca was attributed.

Griffith

The Red Bull bellowing to the kine advances, causing the heavens and earth to roar and tbunder.
Well is he beard like Indra’s shout in battle: letting this voice be known he hastens hither.

Geldner

Der rote Stier, der den K├╝hen entgegenbr├╝llt, geht Erde und Himmel erdr├╢hnend machend. Man h├╢rt seine Stimme wie die Indra┬┤s im Kampfe; er rinnt, indem er diese Rede offenbart.

Grassmann

Der rothe Stier den K├╝h’n entgegenbr├╝llend, geht mit Get├╢n erf├╝llend Erd’ und Himmel, Man h├╢rt im Kampf ihn wie des Indra Brausen, er str├╢mt herbei, auch dieses Lied erweckend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬplural asant to the taste, dripping with milk, you flow pouring forth the sweet-flavoured juice. Soma, when purified and sprinkled, you flow for Indra in a continuous stream.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Good to taste, swelling with milk, you go, setting in motion the
honeyed plant.
Purifying yourself, you go, producing thunder, while being poured
around for Indra, o Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On saс╣Гtan├н- see comm. ad IX.69.2.

Jamison Brereton Notes

No particular signs of cohesion in this tс╣Ыca, which is a collection of soma tropes. If there is any unifying theme it is movement, with eti (13b), eс╣гi (14b, c), arс╣гati (13d), arс╣гa (15d); for other repeated lexical items also pariс╣гicy├бm─Бnaс╕е (14d), p├бri тАж sikt├бс╕е (15d). Also the final vs. (15) begins with ev─Б╠Б, the common hymn-ending summary particle - an effect that is muted in the published translation

The poet is supposed to be Upamanyu V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, presumably following up on the Manyu to whom the last tс╣Ыca was attributed.

Griffith

Swelling with milk, abounding in sweet flavours, urging the meath-rich plant thou goest onward.
Raising a shout thou flowest as they cleanse thee, when thou, O Soma, art effused for Indra.

Geldner

W├╝rzig, von Milch schwellend gehst du, den s├╝├Яen Stengel in Flu├Я bringend. W├дhrend du dich l├дuterst, gibst du den Ton an, wann du f├╝r Indra umgegossen wirst, o Soma.

Gar k├╢stlich schmeckend, strotzend von dem Milchsaft den honigs├╝ssen Saft entsendend gehst du, Get├╢s’ erregend gehst du, hellentflammter, o Soma, rings f├╝r Indra dich ergiessend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThus flow, the exhilarator, for Indra’s exhilaration bowing down the rain-holder with (your) weapons, assuming brilliant colour, desirous of our cattle, flow, Soma, sprinkled (into the filter).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself thus, an exhilarating one for exhilaration, bowing with your weapons (those) of the water-grasper.
Encompassing the glistening color, seeking cows, rush to us, when you are poured around, o Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was noted just above, the hymn-summary quality of the ev─Б╠Бopening this vs. is not sufficiently represented. I would now alter the tr. to тАЬJust in this way purify yourself тАжтАЭ The etym. figure madir├│ m├бd─Бya is reminiscent of matsar├│ m├бd─Бya in the previous tс╣Ыca (11d), and p─Бda-final m├бd─Бya is prominent in the first part of this hymn (5b, 10b, 11d, 15a).

The identity of the тАШwater-grabberтАЩ (uda-gr─Бbh├б-) is unclear. The best suggestion, in my view, is GeldnerтАЩs: Vс╣Ыtra. This interpr. entails an implicit identification of Soma with Indra here, but this is not unprecedented: see for ex. the passages in which Soma is called vс╣Ыtra-h├бn(tama)- (IX.1.3, 24.6), and note that in the 1st vs. of this tс╣Ыca (13c) SomaтАЩs voice is compared to IndraтАЩs. S─Бyaс╣Зa. suggests тАШcloudтАЩ, but why would Soma be fighting a cloud? Oldenberg has an ingenious, ritually oriented solution, whereby udagr─Бbh├б- does not identify the (to-be-)vanquished enemy, but rather the type of weapon Soma is using (the gen. thus depending directly on vadhasna├нh)- namely the ritual ladle (Wassersch├╢pfer). He uses the power of water to vanquish an unexpressed enemy, namely тАЬdie feindlichen M├дchte.тАЭ Although Oldenberg rejects the possibility that udagr─Бbh├б- refers to Vс╣Ыtra, in part because too much would need to be supplied, in fact by his interpr. the hostile object itself would have to be supplied.

His solution also does not mesh with passages like I.165.6 v├н┼Ыvasya ┼Ы├бtror ├бnamam vadhasna├нс╕е тАЬI bowed with my weapons (those) of every rival,тАЭ which has the exact syntactic configuration of our passage.

The expression in p─Бda c, тАЬencompassing the glistening color,тАЭ presumably refers to SomaтАЩs incorporating the gleaming white milk - rendered clearly, if nonliterally, by GeldnerтАЩs тАЬweisse Farbe annehmend.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

No particular signs of cohesion in this tс╣Ыca, which is a collection of soma tropes. If there is any unifying theme it is movement, with eti (13b), eс╣гi (14b, c), arс╣гati (13d), arс╣гa (15d); for other repeated lexical items also pariс╣гicy├бm─Бnaс╕е (14d), p├бri тАж sikt├бс╕е (15d). Also the final vs. (15) begins with ev─Б╠Б, the common hymn-ending summary particle - an effect that is muted in the published translation

The poet is supposed to be Upamanyu V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, presumably following up on the Manyu to whom the last tс╣Ыca was attributed.

Griffith

So flow thou on inspiriting, for rapture, aiming deatb-shafts at him who stays the waters,
Flow to us wearing thy resplendent colour, effused and eager for the kine, O Soma.

So l├дutere dich, berauschend zum Rausche, mit den Schl├дgen die des Wasserfassers parierend. Wei├Яe Farbe annehmend flie├Яe uns, nach den K├╝hen verlangend, wann du umgegossen bist, o Soma!

Grassmann

So riesle flammend denn zur Lust berauschend, den Dieb der Flut mit Keulen niederschmetternd, Ringshin verbreitend deine lichte Farbe, kampflustig, Soma, str├╢m’ uns rings ergossen.

English translation:

тАЬGratified (with our praises), Indu, flow into the large (vessel), granting us riches coming by holy paths and easily acquired; beating down the r─Бkс╣гasas on every side as with a club, flow in a stream upon the elevated fleece.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Having taken pleasure, o drop, (making) easy pathways easy to travel for us, purify yourself on a broad (path), making us wide spaces.
Smashing asunder obstacles to progress as if with a deadly weapon, run along the back, on the sheepтАЩs back.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The vs. contrasts easy travel (a: sup├бth─Б sug─Б╠Бni) with difficult travel (c: durit─Б╠Бni); the contrast is signaled by su- / duс╣г-, while two different roots for тАШgoтАЩ serve as 2nd cmpd. member, тИЪg─Б (or тИЪgam?) versus тИЪi.

The part. kс╣Ыс╣Зv├бn in b should be supplied to govern sup├бth─Б sug─Б╠Бni in a.

Pace Geldner and Renou, I do not think naс╕е should be construed with the ger. juс╣гс╣нv─л╠Б; it is simply in WackernagelтАЩs position and goes better with sup├бth─Б sug─Б╠Бni.

For the loc. ura├║ see III.54.9 ura├║ path├н.

For ghan├йva see comm. ad I.63.5.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca does seem to have a controlling theme and metaphor, esp. in 17-18 – the passage through the filter, beginning in 16. Navigating among the curly tufts is compared on the one hand to the triumphant progress of the Aryas (vs. 17) and to a sort of moral progress in discriminating between the crooked and the straight (18). Each vs. also contains a form of the impv. dhanva тАШrunтАЩ (16d, 17c, 18d).

The Anukramaс╣З─л names Vy─Бghrap─Бd (тАШTigerfoot(ed)тАЩ) V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha as the poet, a colorful name with no precedent in the text.

Griffith

Pleased with us, Indu, send us as thou flowest good easy paths in ample space and comforts.
Dispelling, as ’twere with a club, misfortunes, run o’er the height, run o’er the fleecy summit.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSending us rain from heaven, quick-falling, food-giving, giving health to our home, promptly munificent; flow, Indu, seeking these lower winds your kinsmen as (one seeking his) beloved infants.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Giving health to our home: ┼Ыaс╣Гgay─лm = sakhasya niv─Бsabh┼лtam, inhabiting happiness; the kinsmen: because Indra and the winds are in the relation of praised and praiser; im─Бn v─Бy┼лn = us approaching you, asm─Бn tv─Бm abhigacchataс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Stream rain to usтАФheavenly, hurrying, bringing refreshment, luck for the livestock, of lively drops.
Run, pulling apart [=discriminating] these bonds here below, these
webs, like straightened curls, o drop.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Renou hints, ┼Ыaс╣Гg├бy─л- is a species of univerbation of the common expression ┼Ы├бm + DAT тАЬweal, luck for X.тАЭ The 2nd hemistich of this vs. is very difficult. Decoding it is made somewhat easier by recognizing the governing image: the progress of the Soma in and around the tufts of wool on the sheepskin filter. The Soma is urged to тАШpull apartтАЩ v├н тИЪci the b├бndh┼лn тАШbondsтАЩ; b├бndhu- is multivalent here. It refers on the one hand to the physical bonds that exist between the wool tufts, blocking SomaтАЩs progress. It is notable that in VS 23.36 v├н cinvantu has l├│ma тАШhairтАЩ as object, and refers to the separation of the hair of the sacrificial horse to mark the lines along which the flaying knives are to follow. But b├бndhu- can also refer to bonds of kinship and therefore to kin-groups. Here the 2nd sense of v├н тИЪci, тАШdiscriminateтАЩ, is probably in play, as Soma as representative of ─Аrya progress makes strategic alliances among these groups.

Geldner follows this 2nd interpr. still further by emending the unclear (indo) v─Бy┼л╠Бn to *indav *─Бy┼л╠Бn, tr. тАЬindem du тАж diese n├дchsten Freunde [=b├бndh┼л╠Бn sj], die ─Аyu’s, aussucht.тАЭ In my opinion emending to ─Аyus doesnтАЩt help much, and I donтАЩt think v─Бy┼л╠Бn is as hopeless as he finds it - though I donтАЩt think the path that Oldenberg and Renou follow is a convincing one either. They both take it, reasonably enough, as belonging to the extremely well-attested stem v─Бy├║- тАШwindтАЩ, and Oldenberg suggests that these winds might be rain-bringing, thus relating to the vс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├н- desired in the first hemistich. But this takes us far from the fleece filter and the images it produces. I suggest instead that it is a nonce formation to the pseudo-root тИЪv─Б тАШweaveтАЩ (on which see, e.g., EWA s.v. O, esp. p. 276), meaning тАШwebsтАЩ and again refers to the tangled non-linear paths through the fleece. In this context the тАШweaveтАЩ sense would be available to the audience. Renou hints at a connection with тАШweaveтАЩ in his n., but his tr. doesnтАЩt reflect it.

One of the curious features of this hemistich is that it is the simile that contains the word that is closest to the actual physical object under discussion - namely (*)st├║ka- тАШcurlтАЩ, very close to тАШtuftтАЩ. Before discussing the meaning further, I should comment on the form. The stem of this word is generally given as fem. st├║k─Б-, and there are certainly clear fem. forms (acc. st├║k─Бm AV VII.74.2, also by implication the poss. adj. stuk─Бv├нn- RV VIII.74.13, although the latter could show lengthening at morpheme boundary [cf. dvay─Б-v├нn- and AiG II.2.917-18]). But nothing forbids us from interpr. st├║k─Б here as a neut. pl. to a them. st├║ka- (so already Oldenberg), which immensely aids the interpr. of the passage, since a nom. тАШtuft, curlтАЩ compared to the subj. Soma and commanded to run is close to senseless. One can interpr. the relationship between fem. st├║k─Б- and neut. st├║ka- in one of two ways.

Either the neut. stem was so common in bahuvr─лhis modifying females - e.g., v├нс╣гitastuk─Б тАШwith unloosened curlsтАЩ of Rodas─л in I.167.5 - that the 2nd member was reinterpr. as fem. Or, again because of its presence in bahuvr─лhis modifying females, the originally fem. 2nd member was interpr. as -stuka-, with the fem. gender appropriate only when a fem. was so characterized by a bahuvr─лhi containing it.

Either way, I think we can confidently assume a neut. acc. pl. here, parallel to b├бndh┼лn and v─Бy┼л╠Бn. Soma is urged to pull apart the b├бndh┼лn тАЬlike straightened curls/tufts.тАЭ That v─лt├б- means тАШstraight, straightenedтАЩ is clear from IV.2.11 cited by Geldner: c├нttim ├бcittiс╣Г cinavad v├н vidv─Б╠Бn, pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нh├йva v─лt─Б╠Бvс╣Ыjin─Б╠Бca m├бrt─Бn тАЬInsight and lack of insight will the knowing one [=Agni] distinguish, like backs, straight and crooked, (like) mortals,тАЭ where it is contrasted with vс╣Ыjin├б- тАШcrookedтАЩ, with both acting as object of v├н тИЪci as here. Cf. also the bahuvr. v─лt├б-pс╣Ыс╣гс╣нha- тАШstraight-backedтАЩ, v─лt├б-v─Бra- тАШstraight-tailedтАЩ. This adj. is likely derived from the root тИЪv─л тАШpursueтАЩ, as Grassmann suggests, but seems synchronically distinct from the other uses of the ppl. to this root. Grassmann gives it a separate lemma. Oldenberg suggests that st├║k─Б тАж v─лt─Б╠Бrefers to тАЬKammwolleтАЭ or worsted wool, that is (I learn from the internet), wool yarn that has been combed rather than carded; carded yarn is fuzzier than worsted yarn. Whether this technical interpr. is correct or not, itтАЩs clear that the curls or tufts in question are easier to navigate than those that are not v─лt├б-.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca does seem to have a controlling theme and metaphor, esp. in 17-18 – the passage through the filter, beginning in 16. Navigating among the curly tufts is compared on the one hand to the triumphant progress of the Aryas (vs. 17) and to a sort of moral progress in discriminating between the crooked and the straight (18). Each vs. also contains a form of the impv. dhanva тАШrunтАЩ (16d, 17c, 18d).

The Anukramaс╣З─л names Vy─Бghrap─Бd (тАШTigerfoot(ed)тАЩ) V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha as the poet, a colorful name with no precedent in the text.

Griffith

Pour on us rain celestial, quickly streaming, refreshing, fraught with health and ready bounty.
Flow, Indu, send these Winds thy lower kinsmen, setting them free like locks of hair unbraided.

Geldner

Str├╢me uns den himmlischen Regen her, den eiligen, labenden, dem Hausstand zutr├дglichen, dessen Gabe rasch ist! Rinne, indem du wie die schlichten Wollzotten diese n├дchsten Freunde, die Ayu┬┤s, aussuchst, o Saft!

Grassmann

O str├╢m’ uns her des Himmels schnellen Regen, der reich an Trunk und Thau dem Hause Heil bringt, Gleich grader Rinne str├╢me und verjage, die Winde, Indu, diese schlechten Freunde.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Soma), when filtered loose (me) bound (by sin) as (one loose) a knot; (grant me) a straight path and strength. You, green-tinted, neigh like a horse (when you are) let loose; proceed divine (Soma) who are friendly to man, and have a dwelling.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Untie like a knot the straight and the crooked way that are knotted up, when you are being purified, o Soma.
Like a fallow bay steed you whinny on being let loose; run, o god, as a man in his prime in possession of a dwelling place.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬstraight versus crookedтАЭ theme is continued here, and in fact the expression v─лt─Б╠Бvс╣Ыjin─Б╠Бca тАЬstraight and crookedтАЭ cited from IV.2.11 in the immed.

preceding comm. is lexically renewed (/clarified) by с╣Ыj├║с╣Г ca тАж vс╣Ыjin├бс╣Г ca, with a better attested and unambiguous word for тАШstraightтАЩ, с╣Ыj├║-. Again, SomaтАЩs progress across the tufted filter is the topic, made clearer by the use of g─Бt├║- тАШwayтАЩ. Both Geldner and Renou (also Ober II.60) take the verb v├н с╣гya only with p─Бda a and supply a new verb (тАШdiscriminateтАЩ or the like) with b, relying perhaps too heavily on the model of IV.2.11. I think literal unknotting is whatтАЩs at stake - finding a way between the entangled wool tufts. Geldner further suggests (n. 18a) that the unknotting refers to getting rid of the stalk of the plant in the soma press, but the filter makes far more sense.

The two images in d seem oddly incoherent together: m├бryaс╕е тАж pastiy─Б╠Аv─Бn тАЬa man in his prime in possession of a dwelling place,тАЭ but a passage adduced by Geldner (n. 18d) demonstrates that the young man and the house go together: I.91.13 m├бrya iva sv├б oky├и тАЬ(take pleasure) like a young man in his own home.тАЭ Perhaps the point of the house-proud m├бrya- is that a man in his prime, perhaps roughly the equivalent of the later gс╣Ыhastha, should have achieved the goals of a mature life: a house and household; Soma is implicitly likened to such a man after he has been purified and acquired the water and milk that make him the fully prepared ritual substance, and the pasty─Б╠А- itself is the ritual ground. GeldnerтАЩs parallel also neatly provides indirect evidence for the semantic equivalence of pasty─Б╠А- and oky├а- тАШhomeтАЩ and therefore against the interpr. of pasty─Б╠А- as тАШriverтАЩ (often indeed by Geldner; see, e.g., IX.65.23, though he tr. it here as Haus). See comm. ad I.40.7.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This tс╣Ыca does seem to have a controlling theme and metaphor, esp. in 17-18 – the passage through the filter, beginning in 16. Navigating among the curly tufts is compared on the one hand to the triumphant progress of the Aryas (vs. 17) and to a sort of moral progress in discriminating between the crooked and the straight (18). Each vs. also contains a form of the impv. dhanva тАШrunтАЩ (16d, 17c, 18d).

The Anukramaс╣З─л names Vy─Бghrap─Бd (тАШTigerfoot(ed)тАЩ) V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha as the poet, a colorful name with no precedent in the text.

Griffith

Part, like a knotted tangle, while they cleanse thee, O Soma, righteous and unrighteous conduct.
Neigh like a tawny courser who is loosened, come like a youth, O God, a house-possessor.

Geldner

L├╢se, wenn du dich l├дuterst, das Verknotete wie einen Knoten, scheide den geraden und den krummen Weg, o Soma! Wie ein Hengst m├╢gest du wiehern, wenn du, der Falbe, lossprengst; laufe, o Gott, als junger Mann, der ein eigenes Haus hat aus Pastyavat!

Grassmann

Wie einen Knoten trenne das verschlungne, o Soma, flammend, graden Weg und krummen, Gleich goldnem Renner, der entsandt ist, wieh’re und lauf, o Gott, als starker Hengst des Hauses.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIndu, who are adequate for exhilaration flow in a stream to the elevated fleece at the sacrifice; thousand- streaming, fragrant, irresistible, flow for the acquisition of food in the combat.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Delightful, for the divine conclave for exhilaration, run around the back, on the sheepтАЩs back.
Possessing a thousand streams, sweet-smelling, not to be outwitted, flow around at the winning of prizes, at the victory over
superior men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Attributed to ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who, unlike most of the other Vasiс╣гс╣нhids named by the Anukr. for this hymn, has other vss. attributed to him: VII.32.26, IX.108.3, 14-16. The tс╣Ыca is more concerned with the godsтАЩ consumption of soma than previous ones; note the тАЬdivine conclaveтАЭ (dev├бt─Бte) in 19a, the invitation to the gods to come to the sacrifice to drink soma in 20d, and the pursuit of the gods (dev├бv─лtim) in 21a. The final verse of the tс╣Ыca (21) also begins with a hymnsummarizing ev─Б╠Бand the type of plea for benefits that often end a hymn. The first two vss. of the tс╣Ыca also contain forms of тИЪdhanv: impv. dhanva (19b) and dhanvanti (20c), thus continuing the repeated impv. dhanva of the previous tс╣Ыca - with this concatenation suggesting a reason for attaching this tс╣Ыca here.

Griffith

For the God’s service, for delight, O Indu, run o’er the height, run o’ver the fleecy summit.
With thousand streams, inviolate, sweet-scented, flow on for gain of strength that conquers heroes.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese brilliant Soma juices flow like horses let loose inbattle without reins, without chariots, unharnessed; approach them, you gods, to drink.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Though without reins, without chariot, not yoked, having been let loose like steeds in a contest,
these gleaming soma-drinks run. O gods, drive right up to them, to drink them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation dispenses with the rel. prn. in p─Бda a, as tr. the hemistich as a rel. cl. seemed clunky.

Note the alliteration of ab ara┼Ыm─Б╠Бno y├й arath─Б╠Б├бyukt─Б, ├бty─Бso n├б sasс╣Ыj─Бn─Б╠Бsa ─Бja├║.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Attributed to ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who, unlike most of the other Vasiс╣гс╣нhids named by the Anukr. for this hymn, has other vss. attributed to him: VII.32.26, IX.108.3, 14-16. The tс╣Ыca is more concerned with the godsтАЩ consumption of soma than previous ones; note the тАЬdivine conclaveтАЭ (dev├бt─Бte) in 19a, the invitation to the gods to come to the sacrifice to drink soma in 20d, and the pursuit of the gods (dev├бv─лtim) in 21a. The final verse of the tс╣Ыca (21) also begins with a hymnsummarizing ev─Б╠Бand the type of plea for benefits that often end a hymn. The first two vss. of the tс╣Ыca also contain forms of тИЪdhanv: impv. dhanva (19b) and dhanvanti (20c), thus continuing the repeated impv. dhanva of the previous tс╣Ыca - with this concatenation suggesting a reason for attaching this tс╣Ыca here.

Griffith

Without a car, without a rein to guide them, unyoked, like coursers started in the contest,
These brilliant drops of Soma juice run forward. Do ye, O Deities, come nigh to drink them.

Geldner

Die ohne Z├╝gel, ohne Wagen, ungeschirrt, wie Rennpferde im Wettrennen losgelassen werden, diese klaren Somas├дfte rinnen. Ihr G├╢tter, kommet her, um sie zu trinken!

Grassmann

Wie Renner die beim Wettlauf ohne Wagen unangeschirrt und ohne Z├╝gel laufen, So str├╢men diese hellen Somatr├дnke, zu denen eilt, o G├╢tter, hin zum Trunke.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Attributed to ┼Ъakti V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who, unlike most of the other Vasiс╣гс╣нhids named by the Anukr. for this hymn, has other vss. attributed to him: VII.32.26, IX.108.3, 14-16. The tс╣Ыca is more concerned with the godsтАЩ consumption of soma than previous ones; note the тАЬdivine conclaveтАЭ (dev├бt─Бte) in 19a, the invitation to the gods to come to the sacrifice to drink soma in 20d, and the pursuit of the gods (dev├бv─лtim) in 21a. The final verse of the tс╣Ыca (21) also begins with a hymnsummarizing ev─Б╠Бand the type of plea for benefits that often end a hymn. The first two vss. of the tс╣Ыca also contain forms of тИЪdhanv: impv. dhanva (19b) and dhanvanti (20c), thus continuing the repeated impv. dhanva of the previous tс╣Ыca - with this concatenation suggesting a reason for attaching this tс╣Ыca here.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the praise of the zealous worshipper sanctiies him as that of a noisy (crowd) in front (praises) a distinguished (prince) for the support (he affords); then the cows come to the excellent exhilarating Indu, the lord (of all, abiding) in the pitcher, eager to gratify him (with their milk).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

For the support he affords: dharmaс╣Зi = the reason (nimitta) of the praise; i.e. the duty of acquisition and preservation (or the duty of securing property), yogakс╣гema viс╣гayam karma

Jamison Brereton

When the speech from the mind of the seeker fashioned him [=Soma] on the foundation of the preeminent one [=Agni or Indra?] or
face-to-face with the cattle,
thereupon the cows came to him at will, bellowingтАФto the delightful husband, the drop, in the tub.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I read y├бd─л in p─Бda a as y├бd ─л тАШwhen himтАЩ. Note the parallel ─лm in p─Бda c, before a vowel (─лm ─Бyan), while our ─л occurs before m (─л m├бnaso) and could in principle represent a degeminated *─лm m├бnaso (though I donтАЩt think this is nec.). As Geldner (n. 22ab) implies, the point of this p─Бda is that the ritual speech of the priest-poet essentially creates the sacral drink soma [/god Soma] from the mere juice of the soma plant.

I do not, however, follow GeldnerтАЩs interpr. (in the same n.) of b, as meaning that this speech was roused by the prospect of the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б. I am in fact tempted to follow OldenbergтАЩs rather despairing comment, тАЬDer mystischen Verbr├дmung dieses Gedankens in b weiss ich keine Deutung abzugewinnen.тАЭ He finds the other three p─Бdas clear, with the sense that when speech has fashioned soma (or the milk streams, also possible in OldenbergтАЩs opinion), the milk streams stream to the soma. Accepting this as the overall intent of the verse, I think there is some sense - at least structural sense - that can be wrung from b. To begin with, we must focus on the v─Б. Insofar as I can follow his rendering Geldner implicitly interprets the v─Б as loosely contrasting the fashioning from the mind of the seer with that fashioning under the circumstances set out in b, but his tr. seems to me not really German (тАЬSo oft ihn die Rede aus dem Geiste des schauenden (Sehers) heraus formte oder bei der Entscheidung angesichts des besten St├╝ckes ViehтАЭ). KleinтАЩs rendering (DGRV II.147), which seems to follow the structure envisioned by Geldner though with somewhat different content, does not seem to me to be English either: тАЬWhen speech (arising) from the mind of the seer fashioned (it., viz. soma) or in the establishment (of the worship) in the presence of the best cow.тАЭ Renou at least tries to impose some parallelism between a and b, taking dh├бrmaс╣Зi in b as an infinitive that is roughly parallel to the finite verb t├бkс╣гat in a: тАЬQuand la parole (n├йe) de l’esprit du Voyant eut faconn├й (le soma), ou (quand il s’agissait d’) ├йtablir (le sacrifice) en pr├йsence du plus puissant b├йtail.тАЭ None of these basically clausal or pseudo-clausal interpr. seems to me correct (or even parsable). I instead think that the domain of v─Б is only p─Бda b, and that it is conjoining two locative phrases: jy├йс╣гс╣нhasya тАж dh├бrmaс╣Зi and kс╣г├│r ├бn─лke. If I am correct, we are dealing with an example of inverse v─Б (X v─Б Y), rather than the standard X Y v─Б - a pattern that Klein (DGRV II.139) considers rare but existent. In our case v─Б is inserted in the middle of the first, complex member, giving a pattern X v─Б XтАЩ Y YтАЩ. But at least v─Б would be doing its usual job, conjoining parallel nominal expressions, each consisting of a loc. plus dependent gen. Here each would define the conditions or locations under which the fashioning of p─Бda a occurred. The first of the choices is тАЬon the foundation of the preeminent oneтАЭ; in the published translation I suggest that the preeminent one could be either Agni or Indra, both of whom are elsewhere characterized as jy├йс╣гс╣нha-. I now think this is incorrect. Instead I would invoke the two other expressions in IX with loc. to dh├бrman- + GEN, both с╣Ыt├бsya dh├бrman (IX.7.1, 110.4) тАЬon the foundation of truth.тАЭ Although с╣Ыt├б- does not seem to be qualified as jy├йс╣гс╣нha- elsewhere, тАЬpreeminent truthтАЭ is hardly a jarring expression in RV discourse. Here тАЬon the foundation of preeminent (truth)тАЭ would refer physically to the ritual ground and conceptually to the truth that governs the sacrificial enterprise. See also comm. on the next vs. The other loc. expression is harder to interpr. I will start by saying that I accept the interpr. of kс╣г├║- as тАШcattleтАЩ (тЖР *p┼Ыu-), going back to Bloomfield (IF 25 [1909]), rejected here by Oldenberg, but reaffirmed by Thieme (ZDMG 95 [1941] 347 = KlSch 51), and now generally accepted (see all tr. cited above, as well as EWA s.v.).

But what does тАЬface-to-face with the cattleтАЭ (published translation) or possibly тАЬat the forefront of cattleтАЭ / тАЬin front of cattleтАЭ mean in context (or even, indeed, out of context)? I have two suggestions, though neither of them makes a neat disjunctive pair with the first loc. phrase. The stronger suggestion is that this is a temporal expression, referring to dawn. The stem ├бn─лka- is several times used in this way; cf. VI.47.5 (with loc.) uс╣г├бs─Бm ├бn─лke тАЬat the forefront of the dawns,тАЭ V.76.1 uс╣г├бs─Бm ├бn─лkam тАЬthe face of the dawns.тАЭ Esp. apposite for our passage is I.124.11 yuс╣Еkt├й g├бv─Бm aruс╣З─Б╠Бn─Бm ├бn─лkam тАЬShe [=Dawn] yokes the forefront of the ruddy cows,тАЭ with the cows a reference to the reddish rays of dawn. Since Dawn and her rays are frequently assimilated to cows and ├бn─лka- is used to indicate the moment of the appearance of dawn / dawnтАЩs rays, a shorthand expression тАЬat the forefront of the cattleтАЭ could, it seems to me, be a way of saying тАЬat dawn.тАЭ This would make the two locative phrases conjoined by v─Б conceptually non-parallel (though still syntactically parallel), but I think this looseness is within acceptable limits, as offering two alternative ways of identifying the circumstances of the fashioning of Soma by speech: тАЬon the foundation of preeminent (truth) or at the forefront of cattle [=dawn].тАЭ I would now emend the tr.

in that way. Alternatively тАЬin front of cattleтАЭ could refer to the place on the ritual ground where Soma encounters the milk mixture - which milk then comes to him.

This would more narrowly define the location than the first locative phrase, which gives the whole ritual ground as the locus. The 2nd possibility provides a better set of parallels with v─Б - both locational - but I prefer the 1st because of the use of ├бn─лkawith dawn elsewhere.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Karс╣Зa┼Ыrut V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, a name that has no source in the text and is not otherwise found in the Anukr. This tс╣Ыca depicts Soma as a king on a royal journey, and associates him with the resonant words с╣Ыt├б- (23b, 24d) and dh├бrman- (22b) / dharm├бn- (23c) and the traditional roles they imply.

Griffith

What time the loving spirit’s word had formed him Chief of all food, by statute of the Highest,
Then loudly lowing came the cows to Indu, the chosen, well-loved Master in the beaker.

Geldner

So oft ihn die Rede aus dem Geiste des schauenden Sehers heraus formte oder bei der Entscheidung angesichts des besten St├╝ckes Vieh, da kamen nach Wunsch zu dem Safte als dem beliebten Gatten voll Verlangen die K├╝he in dem Kruge.

Grassmann

Als ihn voll Liebe schuf das Wort des Geistes, wie in des H├╢chsten Reich, im Sitz der Speise, Da gingen jauchzend wie zum lieben Gatten voll Lust die K├╝he in dem Kelch zu Indu.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe divine benefactor of givers, poured (boons) on givers, the intelligent (Soma) distils his true beverage for true (Indra); the radiant (Soma) is the upholder of strength, he is entirely restrained by the ten fingers.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The divine giver of drops, sweller of drops, (goes) forth. As truth, he purifies himself for truth, the very wise one.
Possessing the (royal) mandate, he has become the king of what belongs to the community. He has been brought forward to the earth by the ten reins.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Since тИЪp┼л does not appear with pr├б, itтАЩs best to supply a verb of motion with the pr├б opening p─Бda a and take b (with pavate) separately. Note the alliteration in p─Бda a тАж d─Бnud├│ divy├│ d─Бnu(-pinv├бс╕е).

This vs. identifies Soma as тАШtruthтАЩ (с╣Ыt├бm b) and also contains in c the possessive internal deriv. dharm├бn- to dh├бrman-. If I am correct that jy├йс╣гс╣нhasya тАж dh├бrmaс╣Зi in the immed. preceding vs. 22b should be interpr. тАЬon the foundation of preeminent (truth – с╣Ыt├бsya), both resonant words, с╣Ыt├б- and dh├бrman-/dharm├бn-, were already implicitly present in the previous vs. In 23 Soma is then depicted as the embodiment of these words (cf. GeldnerтАЩs тАЬdas (verk├╢rperte) GesetzтАЭ for с╣Ыt├бm), and they define his kingship (r─Б╠Бj─Б in c, also in 24b). Unfortunately it does not seem possible to signal the dh├бrman- / dharm├бn- connection in English tr., but тАШpossessor of the (royal) mandateтАЩ may be too specialized for the latter. Perhaps better тАШfounder, foundation-giver, institutor, maintainerтАЩ. On Soma as тАЬtruthтАЭ see also IX.107.15 and IX.108.8.

The ten reins are presumably the fingers of the presser, as is usual for ten anything in IX.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. each contain the injunc. (/subj.) aor. bhuvat, which in both cases I tr. as an immed. past: тАЬhe has become.тАЭ After considerable disc. with Ian Hollenbaugh, I now think that this particular form can also express a generic or habitual role or behavior of the subject, which Ian Hollenbaugh felicitously renders with the colloquial тАЬhe be-s X.тАЭ I am therefore now inclined to alter the tr. of both vss. to тАЬhe is the king тАжтАЭ / тАЬhe is, now as before, the wealth-lord тАжтАЭ In the absence of a non-colloquial Engl.

habitual/generic, тАЬisтАЭ will have to do.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Karс╣Зa┼Ыrut V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, a name that has no source in the text and is not otherwise found in the Anukr. This tс╣Ыca depicts Soma as a king on a royal journey, and associates him with the resonant words с╣Ыt├б- (23b, 24d) and dh├бrman- (22b) / dharm├бn- (23c) and the traditional roles they imply.

Griffith

The Sage, Celestial, liberal, raining bounties, pours as he flows the Genuine for the Truthful.
The King shall be effectual strength’s upholder: he by the ten bright reins is mostly guided.

Geldner

Der himmlische Gabenspender str├╢mt gabenschwellend hervor; der Weise, das verk├╢rperte Gesetz, l├дutert sich f├╝r die Opfersatzung. Er ward der ma├Яgebende K├╢nig eines jeden, der zur Opfergemeinschaft geh├╢rt. Mit zehn Z├╝geln ward er reichlich vorangebracht.

Grassmann

Des Himmels weiser Tr├дufler, reichlich tr├дufelnder ergiesst den heil’gen Saft dem heil’gen Gotte; Der Ortsgemeinde F├╝rst ist er und Ordner; zehn Z├╝gel haben ihn gelenkt zur Erde.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPurified by the filters the observers of man, the sovereign of both gods and mortals, the lord of abundant wealth (Soma), is twofold; Indu bears the auspicious collected water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Soma is twofold: i.e., abides among both gods and men

Jamison Brereton

Purifying himself with the filters, having his gaze on men, as the king of gods and mortals
he has become once again the wealth-lord of wealth; the drop bears the pleasing truth that is easy to bear.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The two words making up the VP in d, с╣Ыt├бm bharat, appear also in vs. 23, though not together (с╣Ыt├бm с╣Ыt─Б╠Бya b, bh─Бri d). As is pointed out by Hoffmann (implicitly: Injunc. 122 and esp. n. 34) and Ober (II.121), this appears to be an Indo-Iranian phrase, and it thus invests Soma with yet more traditional dignity. The p─Бda thus deserves a more solemn tr. than I gave it in the published translation - perhaps тАЬthe drop bears the dear truth that is well worth the bearing.тАЭ Although the morphological means are different, the lexical duplication in both rayip├бt─л ray─лс╣З─Б╠Бm (c) and с╣Ыt├бm bharat s├║bhс╣Ыtam (d) gives the end of this tс╣Ыca a stately and archaic air.

Jamison Brereton Notes

These two vss. each contain the injunc. (/subj.) aor. bhuvat, which in both cases I tr. as an immed. past: тАЬhe has become.тАЭ After considerable disc. with Ian Hollenbaugh, I now think that this particular form can also express a generic or habitual role or behavior of the subject, which Ian Hollenbaugh felicitously renders with the colloquial тАЬhe be-s X.тАЭ I am therefore now inclined to alter the tr. of both vss. to тАЬhe is the king тАжтАЭ / тАЬhe is, now as before, the wealth-lord тАжтАЭ In the absence of a non-colloquial Engl.

habitual/generic, тАЬisтАЭ will have to do.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Karс╣Зa┼Ыrut V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, a name that has no source in the text and is not otherwise found in the Anukr. This tс╣Ыca depicts Soma as a king on a royal journey, and associates him with the resonant words с╣Ыt├б- (23b, 24d) and dh├бrman- (22b) / dharm├бn- (23c) and the traditional roles they imply.

Griffith

He who beholds mankind, made pure with filters, the King supreme of Deities and mortals,
From days of old is Treasure-Lord of riches: he, Indu, cherishes fair well-kept Order.

English translation:

тАЬHasten (Soma) to give food to Indra and V─Бyu like a horse, for (the sake of giving us) food, to acquire wealth; give us abundant thousand-fold food; Soma, when filtered become the dispenser of riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like a steed rushing to a win for the sake of fame, rush to the pursuit of Indra and V─Бyu.
Give us a thousand lofty refreshments; become a finder of chattels while you are being purified, o Soma. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Like the tс╣Ыca 19-21, this one focuses in great part on the gods as drinkers of soma and the desire to bring them to the ritual; the тАЬpursuitтАЭ (v─лt├нm) of Indra and V─Бyu in 25b is reprised in dev─Б-v─л╠Б- тАШpursuing the godsтАЩ in 26a, while the gods are mentioned twice in 27ab. The final vs. also begins with the typical hymnsummarizing ev─Б╠Бas three times elsewhere in this hymn (vss. 13-15, 19-21, 34-36).

The poet is named as Mс╣Ыс╕Н─лka V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who is also the poet of X.150. In the latter hymn his name is clearly drawn from the dat. mс╣Ыс╕Н─лk─Б╠Бya found in the refrain of every vs., but there is no such basis here.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the Soma juices which are gratifying to the gods when poured around (into the vessels) bring us a dwelling and male offspring– (the juice) endeavouring to gain the favour (of the gods), desired by all offering (to the gods) in heaven like the ministrant priests, most exhilarating.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Endeavouring to gain the favour of the gods: ─Бyajyavaс╕е sumatim vi┼Ыvav─Бr─Бс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Pursuing the gods while being poured around, let the soma drinks run to a dwelling place rich in good heroes,
bringing favor here through sacrifice, possessing all desirable things, sacrificing at day(break) like Hotars, most gladdening.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation omits the enclitic naс╕е; it should be revised to тАЬPursuing the gods for us while тАжтАЭ Geldner takes kс╣г├бyam in b as an Inhaltsakk. (тАЬтАж sollen тАж ein Haus тАж herstr├╢menтАЭ (sim. but more elaborate, Renou). But a dwelling place is a particularly unlikely object to тАЬstream,тАЭ and I prefer to see it as goal (as also Scarlatta 398).

The hapax in d, diviy├бj-, has (at least) two possible meanings: тАШsacrificing at day(break)тАЩ as I take it, and тАШsacrificing (to the gods) in heavenтАЩ (so Geldner, Renou). See GeldnerтАЩs n. and Scarlatta (398-99). There is nothing in the context that tips the balance one way or the other; I prefer the temporal reading because the other one requires more material to be understood. The word also appears in a metrically disturbed p─Бda; as it stands it has 12 syllables and a cadence (- тПС тПС ├Ч) that is bad for both Triс╣гс╣нubh and Jagat─л. Oldenberg suggests the possibility of reading the 1st member of diviy├бj- as a monosyllable, either *divy├бjaс╕е or *dyuy├бjaс╕е, which would at least produce an 11-syl.

line, and these possibilities are disc. in more detail by Scarlatta without a firm conclusion.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Like the tс╣Ыca 19-21, this one focuses in great part on the gods as drinkers of soma and the desire to bring them to the ritual; the тАЬpursuitтАЭ (v─лt├нm) of Indra and V─Бyu in 25b is reprised in dev─Б-v─л╠Б- тАШpursuing the godsтАЩ in 26a, while the gods are mentioned twice in 27ab. The final vs. also begins with the typical hymnsummarizing ev─Б╠Бas three times elsewhere in this hymn (vss. 13-15, 19-21, 34-36).

The poet is named as Mс╣Ыс╕Н─лka V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who is also the poet of X.150. In the latter hymn his name is clearly drawn from the dat. mс╣Ыс╕Н─лk─Б╠Бya found in the refrain of every vs., but there is no such basis here.

Griffith

Effused by us let God-delighting Somas bring as they flow a home with noble heroes.
Rich in all boons like priests acquiring favour, the worshippers of heaven, the best of Cheerers.

G├╢ttereinladend sollen die eingegossenen Somas├дfte uns ein Haus mit t├╝chtigen S├╢hnen herstr├╢men, Gunst erbittend, allbegehrt, gleich den Hotri┬┤s die G├╢tter im Himmel verehrend, sehr erfreuend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬDivine Soma, who are the beverage of the gods, flow at the sacrifice for (their) abundant food; urged on (by you) may we overcome even mighty (foes) in battle; purified do you render heaven and earth happy abodes (for us).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Thus, o god Soma, purify yourself for the conclave of gods, for their great delight, as the godsтАЩ drink,
for we are greatly driven at the encounter. Make the two world-halves of good standing while you are being purified.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The summary ev─Б╠Бmight be more emphatically rendered as тАЬin just this wayтАЭ or sim. The тАЬconclave of the godsтАЭ (dev├бt─Бte) returns from 19a. As Geldner points out, the whole hemistich is almost identical to IX.96.3, save for ev─Б╠Бin place of s├б naс╕е and devap─Б╠Бnaс╕е for indrap─Б╠Бnaс╕е.

The ppl. in the periphrasis in d, sm├бsi hit─Б╠Бс╕е, could belong either to тИЪdh─Б or to тИЪhi (so S─Бyaс╣Зa.). It is actually not clear to me which one Geldner favors from his тАЬdenn wir sind in grossem Wettstreit begriffenтАЭ (and his n. 27c doesnтАЩt entirely clarify). Renou clear chose тИЪdh─Б: тАЬAvec ambition [mah├б┼Ы cid?] nous nous sommes en v├йrit├й plac├й┼Ы dans la comp├йtition.тАЭ I favor тИЪhi: I think the point is that we are тАЬdrivenтАЭ / тАЬhardpressedтАЭ in the hostile encounter, and we need divine help - which we will only get once they have partaken of our soma. But there are several logical steps missing in every interpr.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Like the tс╣Ыca 19-21, this one focuses in great part on the gods as drinkers of soma and the desire to bring them to the ritual; the тАЬpursuitтАЭ (v─лt├нm) of Indra and V─Бyu in 25b is reprised in dev─Б-v─л╠Б- тАШpursuing the godsтАЩ in 26a, while the gods are mentioned twice in 27ab. The final vs. also begins with the typical hymnsummarizing ev─Б╠Бas three times elsewhere in this hymn (vss. 13-15, 19-21, 34-36).

The poet is named as Mс╣Ыс╕Н─лka V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who is also the poet of X.150. In the latter hymn his name is clearly drawn from the dat. mс╣Ыс╕Н─лk─Б╠Бya found in the refrain of every vs., but there is no such basis here.

Griffith

So, God, for service of the Gods flow onward, flow, drink of Gods, for ample food, O Soma.
For we go forth to war against the mighty make heaven and earth well stablished by thy cleansing.

Geldner

So l├дutere dich, o Gott, f├╝r die G├╢tterschaft zu hohem Genu├Я, als der G├╢tter Getr├дnk, o Soma, denn wir sind in gro├Яem Wettstreit begriffen. Setze beide Welten in guten Stand, indem du dich l├дuterst!

Grassmann

So riesle hell, o Gott, der Schar der G├╢tter zum grossen Schmaus, o Soma, gottgetrunken, Denn hoch sind wir geachtet bei dem Feste, mach, flammender, feststehend Erd’ und Himmel.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYoked by the priests, you neigh like a horse, (you are) terrible as a lion, swifter than thought; Indu, pour happiness upon us by those which are the most direct of the paths leading hitherward.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like a horse you whinny on being yoked by the bulls, fearsome like a lion, swifter than mind. Along paths turned hitherwardsтАФthose which are the straightestтАФ
bring benevolence here to us by purifying yourself, o drop.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The opening of the vs., ├б┼Ыvo n├б kradaс╕е, is very close to 18c ├бtyo n├б kradaс╕е. The first hemistich contains three animals, incl. the fairly rare lion. Geldner, fld.

by Renou, identifies the bulls as the priests.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Attributed to Vasukra V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who is not otherwise known - though a Vasukra Aindra is supposedly responsible for the devilish trio of hymns X.27-29.

The tс╣Ыca is marked by the repetition of ─Б╠Бpavasva in the 2nd hemistich of each vs. (28d, 29c, 30d) expressing the various good things we want Soma to bring us through his self-purification. The root тИЪsс╣Ыj тАШsurgeтАЩ is also prominent in the 2nd two vss. (29a, 30a).

Griffith

Thou, yoked by strong men, neighest like a courser, swifter than thought is, like an awful lion.
By paths directed hitherward, the straightest, send thou us happiness, Indu, while they cleanse thee.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour hundred streams manifested for the gods are loose; the sages cleanse those thousand (streams); pour wealth upon us, Indu, from heaven; you are the precursor of abundant riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

A hundred god-generated streams have been sent surging; these thousand the poets groom.
O drop, by purifying yourself bring here from heaven a means of
winning. You are the leader of great spoils.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the hapax san├нtra- in its full lexical value, as a тАШmeans of winningтАЩ, rather than the bleached Spende, Gabe (Grassmann), Lohn (Geldner), le b├йn├йfice (Renou) that prevails. On the accent of the word (and other -tra-stems to seс╣н roots), see AiG II.2.701-2, which also glosses the word as I do: тАШMittel des GewinnensтАЩ, flg. Ludwig.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Attributed to Vasukra V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who is not otherwise known - though a Vasukra Aindra is supposedly responsible for the devilish trio of hymns X.27-29.

The tс╣Ыca is marked by the repetition of ─Б╠Бpavasva in the 2nd hemistich of each vs. (28d, 29c, 30d) expressing the various good things we want Soma to bring us through his self-purification. The root тИЪsс╣Ыj тАШsurgeтАЩ is also prominent in the 2nd two vss. (29a, 30a).

Griffith

Sprung from the Gods, a hundred streams, a thousand, have been effused: sages prepare and purge them.
Bring us from heaven the means of winnning, Indu; thou art-forerunnner of abundant riches.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAs the rays of the days of the sun are let loose (so are the streams of the Soma); a prudent king does not abandon his friend; as a son preserving in pious acts (wins) his father’s (safety), do you pour upon this people immunity from defeat.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Like surges from heaven, (like those) of days, his surges have surged. Like a king, the wise one does not violate his alliance.
Being put in your place according to our intentions, like a son
according to the intentions of his father, bring freedom from
overthrow here to this clan by purifying yourself.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take ├бhn─Бm as a 2nd, unmarked simile dependent on s├бrg─Бс╕е, rather than supplying a different headnoun, as Geldner and Renou do. They are surely both right that тАЬthe surges of/from heavenтАЭ are the rains. As for тАЬthe surges of the days,тАЭ this could either refer to the passage of time or to an abundance of light; I favor the former.

In b n├б should be read as both the simile particle and the negation; see Oldenberg

P─Бdas b-c show a clever chaining of significant vocabulary. In b Soma is compared to a king who doesnтАЩt violate his alliance, with mitr├б- in its common noun usage. But d contains the part. yat─Бn├б- тАШtaking oneтАЩs place, being put in placeтАЩ, and тИЪyat is an action esp. associated with the god Mitra. Cf., e.g., VII.36.2 j├бnaс╣Г ca mitr├│ yatati тАЬMitra puts the people in their placeтАЭ (sim. III.59.1). Although Mitra is not explicitly present here, the lexical continuity might evoke him. It is indeed possible that it is MitraтАЩs intentions (or those of the alliance itself) acdg. to which Soma takes his place, rather than тАЬoursтАЭ as in the published translation

The vs. ends with yet another term relating to social life, namely v├н┼Ы- тАШclanтАЩ; as king, Soma would exert himself on behalf of this social unit.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Attributed to Vasukra V─Бsiс╣гс╣нha, who is not otherwise known - though a Vasukra Aindra is supposedly responsible for the devilish trio of hymns X.27-29.

The tс╣Ыca is marked by the repetition of ─Б╠Бpavasva in the 2nd hemistich of each vs. (28d, 29c, 30d) expressing the various good things we want Soma to bring us through his self-purification. The root тИЪsс╣Ыj тАШsurgeтАЩ is also prominent in the 2nd two vss. (29a, 30a).

The streams of days, were poured as ’twere from heaven: the wise King doth not treat his friend unkindly.
