Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYour exhilarating streams are let loose when you pass purified through the woollen fleece; Pavam─Бna you flow to the supporting (milk) of the kine, as soon as genitive rated you fill the sun with your radiance.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your honeyed streams have surged forth, when, purified, you go across the sheepтАЩs fleece.
Self-purifying one, purify yourself as the domain for the cows. On being born, you swelled the sun with rays [/chants]. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
31-33 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The first vs. of the tс╣Ыca contains a form of тИЪsс╣Ыj, thus concatenating with the previous tс╣Ыca. Both the first (31) and last (33) vss. contain a reference to the sun, and I see one in the middle vs. as well; see comm. ad 32.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The skeleton of p─Бda a, (pr├б te) dh─Б╠Бr─Б (m├бdhumat─лr) asс╣Ыgran, is identical to 29a (┼Ыat├бс╣Г) dh─Б╠Бr─Б (dev├бj─Бt─Б) asс╣Ыgran.

The published translation renders p├бvase as if it were an imperative; correct to тАЬyou purify yourself.тАЭ I take тАЬdomain of cowsтАЭ (dh─Б╠Бma g├│n─Бm) in c to indicate that Soma is the substance into which the milk is mixed. Since the milk is sometimes identified as the sun, his swelling of the sun in d may refer to SomaтАЩs providing more body and amplitude to the milk.

As often, ark├б- can be read as a pun.

Griffith

Now are thy streams poured forth with all their sweetness, when, purified. thou goest through the filter.
The race of kine is thy gift, Pavarridna: when born thou madest Surya rich with brightness.

Geldner

Deine s├╝├Яen Str├╢me haben sich ergossen, w├дhrend du gel├дutert durch die Schafhaare gehst. O Pavamana, du l├дuterst dich als Essenz der K├╝he. Sobald du geboren wardst, hast du die Sonne mit Strahlen angeschwellt.

Grassmann

Ergossen sind jetzt deine, s├╝ssen Str├╢me, da du gereinigt durch die Wolle schreitest, Hellflammend str├╢mst du zu der K├╝he St├дtte; geboren f├╝lltest du mit Licht die Sonne.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(The Soma) cries repeatedly upon the path of the sacrifice; you shine (being) the abode of immortality; possessing exhilaration you flow for Indra, sending forth your voice with the praises of the sages.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Ever roaring along the path of truth, gleaming you radiate across the domain of the immortal one [=sun?].
Providing the means for exhilaration, you purify yourself for Indra,
spurring on your own speech with the thoughts of the poets.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬdomain for the cowsтАЭ is echoed here by the тАЬdomain of the immortal oneтАЭ (amс╣Ы╠Бtasya dh─Б╠Бma). As with the same phrase in IX.94.2 (q.v.), I suggest that the immortal one is the sun, and perhaps specifically milk as representative of the sun.

The role of the sun in the surrounding vss. (31d, 33d) supports this interpr. For alternative interpr. of the phrase, see comm. ad IX.94.2. In our passage Renou (sim. L├╝ders 467) suggests that it is actually nom. and refers to Soma, but in IX.94.2 it must be an acc. obj. (also acdg. to Renou).

The cadence of c is bad as transmitted, but can be easily fixed by reading

*matsar─Б-v─Бn with the common lengthening of the stem vowel -a- before -vant- and -van-; see Oldenberg, in agreement with Arnold. The stem is a hapax, and it is clearly a morphological variant of matsar├нn(-tama)- (4x), with a different possessive suffix. In fact, our p─Бda is a nonce Triс╣гс╣нubh adaptation of the Jagat─л line IX.76.5 s├б ├нndr─Бya pavase matsar├нntamaс╕е. For further disc. see comm. ad IX.76.5. The interchangeability of -vant- and -├нn- for metrical purposes speaks against the two possessive suffixes having crucial functional differences.

The initial s├б in both our p─Бda and the one on which it is based does not follow my rules for s├б 2nd-ps. reference. On this aberrancy see comm. ad IX.76.5, where it can be motivated. That p─Бda was then simply borrowed (and slightly altered) here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first vs. of the tс╣Ыca contains a form of тИЪsс╣Ыj, thus concatenating with the previous tс╣Ыca. Both the first (31) and last (33) vss. contain a reference to the sun, and I see one in the middle vs. as well; see comm. ad 32.

Griffith

Bright, bellowing aiong the path of Order, thou shinest as the form of life eternal.
Thou flowest on as gladdening drink for Indra, sending thy voice out with the hymns of sages.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSoma, who are celestial, well-winged, you look down from heaven, pouring forth your streams by the pious rite at the sacrifice; Indu, enter into the pitcher the receptacle of the Soma; crying aloud approach the sun’s rays.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Look down from heaven: avacakс╣гi, an imperative

Jamison Brereton

As heavenly eagle, o Soma, gaze down, swelling the streams with (ritual) action in the pursuit of the gods.
O drop, enter the tub for holding the soma. Roaring, come right up to the ray of the sun.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The form cakс╣гi (also VII.3.6) is in both of its occurrences pretty clearly an impv., but its formation is something of a puzzle. It appears to be a -si impv. (so Baum, Imperative, 46, 107, with no disc.), but it has none of the standard supports for such a form. Not only does it not have an s-aor. subjunctive, but it has no aorist forms at all, and almost all the occurrences of its well-attested root pres. are medial.

And of course, assuming it belongs to тИЪcakс╣г, the form would have to be degeminated from *cakс╣г-с╣гi (though that would not be hard). The parallel passage IX.71.9 has a medial injunc. to the marginal thematic stem (see Hoffmann 122 n. 33): divy├бс╕е suparс╣З├│ ‘va cakс╣гata kс╣г─Б╠Бm. I have no explanation for this aberrant form; it is true that the proper med. impv. to the root pres. cakс╣гva (3x) would not fit this metrical slot, but that doesnтАЩt seem reason enough to invent cakс╣гi.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first vs. of the tс╣Ыca contains a form of тИЪsс╣Ыj, thus concatenating with the previous tс╣Ыca. Both the first (31) and last (33) vss. contain a reference to the sun, and I see one in the middle vs. as well; see comm. ad 32.

Griffith

Pouring out streams at the Gods’ feast with service, thou, Soma, lookest down, a heavenly Eagle.
Enter the Soma-holding beaker, Indu, and with a roar approach the ray of Sarya.

Geldner

Als himmlischer Adler blicke herab, o Soma, deine Str├╢me mit dem Opferwerk befruchtend bei der G├╢tterladung! Geh, o Saft, in den somafassenden Krug ein, geh br├╝llend bis zum Strahl der Sonne!

Grassmann

Des Himmels Adler wird erblickt, o Soma, die Str├╢me schwellend durch sein Werk beim Festmahl, Geh ein, o Indu, in die Somakufe und eile wiehernd zu dem Strahl der Sonne.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe bearer (of the oblation) utters the three praises, the thought of Brahma that sustains the sacrifice; the kine come to the cowherd asking (to be milked), the praisers proceed to the Soma with eagerness.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The bearer of the oblation: i.e., the worshipper; the three texts are: с╣Ыk, yajus. and s─Бman;

Brahmaс╣Зaс╕е = the spureme, parivс╣Ыс╕Нhasya Soma; the kine come to Soma to mix their milk with him

Jamison Brereton

The draft-horse rouses forth the three voices, the hymnic vision of truth, the inspired thought of the sacred formulation.
The cows go asking for a cowherd; the thoughts go bellowing eagerly to Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the тАЬthree voicesтАЭ (tisr├│ v─Б╠Бcaс╕е) see comm. ad IX.33.4, 50.2.

The parallel expressions in c and d – тАж yanti тАж PTCLE contrast the progress of ritual substance (milk) and ritual speech (thoughts). As elsewhere, v─Бva┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е could belong to both тИЪv─Б┼Ы тАШbellowтАЩ and тИЪva┼Ы тАШdesire, be eagerтАЩ (cf. IX.93.4, 95.4).

Given the emphasis on noise in this tс╣Ыca, the former is probably primary, but both can be meant - hence my tr. тАЬbellowing eagerly.тАЭ

34-36 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

All three vss. concentrate on ritual speech and on the noisy approach of both cows and poets to Soma. This theme takes up 32d, where Soma impels his own speech in concert with the productions of the poets. The final vs., 36, begins with hymn-summarizing ev─Б╠Б.

Griffith

Three are the voices that the Courser utters: he speaks the thought of prayer, the law of Order.
To the Cow’s Master come the Cows inquiring: the hymns with eager longing come to Soma.

Geldner

Drei Stimmen setzt der Wagenlenker in Bewegung, die Erkenntnis des Gesetzes, den Gedanken der heiligen Rede. Die K├╝he kommen, sich nach dem Kuhherrn zu erkundigen, zu Soma kommen verlangend die Dichtungen.

Grassmann

Drei Stimmen sind es, die der Fahrer anregt, als Brauch des Opfers, als Gebetes Andacht; Die K├╝he gehn zum Herrn der K├╝he flehend, zum Soma gehen rauschend die Gebete.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe kine (are) longing for the Soma; wise men (are) inquiring for him with praises; Soma being effused is purified blended (with milk), our adorations in the triс╣гс╣нubh metre are united in the Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To Soma (go) the milk-cows bellowing eagerly; to Soma the inspired poets asking for him with their thoughts.
Soma, pressed, is purified while being anointed [/driven]; to Soma the chants, the triс╣гс╣нubh verses cry out together.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first two p─Бdas of this vs. are variants of the last two of the previous vs. (34cd), with the repeated yanti of 34 gapped, and redistribution of some of the lexicon: the two participles in 34cd, prch├бm─Бn─Бс╕е and v─Бva┼Ы─Бn─Б╠Бс╕е, switch positions, with each paired with a more natural subject (cows bellowing 35a, poets asking 35b), and the thoughts of 34d are relegated to the instr. in 35b with their producers, the vipr─Б╠Бс╕е, taking over the subject role in 35b, again a more natural configuration. We can consider 35ab as a complex poetic repair of 34cd.

34-36 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

All three vss. concentrate on ritual speech and on the noisy approach of both cows and poets to Soma. This theme takes up 32d, where Soma impels his own speech in concert with the productions of the poets. The final vs., 36, begins with hymn-summarizing ev─Б╠Б.

Griffith

To Soma come the Cows, the Milch-kine longing, to Soma sages with their hvmns inquiring.
Soma, effused, is purified and blended our hymns and Trstup songs unite in Soma.

Zum Soma kommen die Milchk├╝he verlangend, br├╝llend, zum Soma sich befragend kommen mit Gebeten die Redekundigen. Der ausgepre├Яte Soma wird gel├дutert, indem er gesalbt wird. In den Soma stimmen zusammen die Loblieder, die Tristubh┬┤s ein.

Grassmann

Zum Soma gehen rauschend hin die K├╝he, zum Soma S├дnger mit Gebeten flehend; Gepresst, gesalbet und gekl├дrt wird Soma, in Soma gehn dreistimmig ein die Lieder.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThus poured around (into the vessels), Soma, do you when purified flow for our welfare, enter with a great noise into Indra, foster our praise, genitive rate abundant knowledge in us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With great noise: S─Бmaveda has madena for raveс╣Зa

Jamison Brereton

Thus, o Soma, being poured around, being purified, bring well-being here to us through your purification.
Enter Indra with a lofty shout; strengthen speech, beget plenitude.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The hymn-summary ev─Б╠Бcould once again be rendered more forcefully: тАЬin just this wayтАЭ vel sim.

34-36 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

All three vss. concentrate on ritual speech and on the noisy approach of both cows and poets to Soma. This theme takes up 32d, where Soma impels his own speech in concert with the productions of the poets. The final vs., 36, begins with hymn-summarizing ev─Б╠Б.

Griffith

Thus, Soma, as we pour thee into vessels, while thou art purified flow for our welfare.
Pass into Indra with a mighty roaring make the voice swell, and generate abundance.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe vigilant Soma, the knower of true praises, being purified, has sat down in the vessels– (the Soma) whom the adhvaryus touch, combined, emulous, leaders of the sacrifice, auspicious-handed.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Touch: sapati spс╣Ы┼Ыatikarm─Б (Nirukta 5.16)

Jamison Brereton

In accordance with truth, the wakeful inspired poet of the thoughts, Soma, being purified, has sat down in the cups,
he whom they serve, eager in rivalryтАФthe Adhvaryus of good hands, the charioteers (of the sacrifice).

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a v├нpraс╕е тАж mat─лn─Б╠Бm reprises v├нpr─Б mat├нbhiс╕е of 35b in concatenary fashion. For further on this phrase see below.

Grassmann, Geldner, and Renou, as well as L├╝ders (439), take с╣Ыt─Б╠Бas neut. pl., but this disturbs the syntax, and the tr. all must supply a verb to govern it. I suggest that it is instead the instr. sg. Renou explicitly rejects this possibility on the grounds that it would be morphologically isolated. If he means that it would be the only such instr. to this stem, he seems to be correct, but given that the -─Б instr. to them. stems is in retreat, this isolation would not be surprising. If he means that them. neuters donтАЩt have instr.

in -─Б, this is not correct: Lanman (Noun infl., 335) considers them more frequent than to the masc. and counts 77. Whether all his exx. would hold up under closer scrutiny is irrelevant: 77 would be difficult to reduce to 0.

The standard tr. also construe gen. pl. mat─лn─Б╠Бm with с╣Ыt─Б╠Б, whatever sense they ascribe to с╣Ыt─Б╠Б, e.g., Geldner тАЬdie rechten Wege der Gedanken,тАЭ L├╝ders тАЬzu den Wahrheiten der Gedanken.тАЭ They may be correct, and I could revise my tr. accordingly: тАЬIn accordance with the truth of the thoughts, Soma тАжтАЭ However, the association of v├нpra- with mat├н- is very strong - I just noted it in 35b in the previous tс╣Ыca, and the two words occur in the same p─Бda numerous times: I.82.2=VIII.25.24 v├нpr─Б тАж mat─л╠Б, I.86.2 v├нprasya тАж mat─лn─Б╠Бm, II.24.13 v├нpraс╕е тАж mat─л╠Б, III.5.3 v├нpraс╕е тАж mat─лn─Б╠Бm, III.30.20=50.4 mat├нbhiс╕е тАж v├нpr─Бс╕е, IV.3.16 mat├нbhir v├нpraс╕е, V.80.1 v├нpr─Бso mat├нbhiс╕е, VII.78.2 v├нpr─Бso mat├нbhiс╕е, IX.63.21 mat─л╠Бv├нpr─Бс╕е, IX.85.7 v├нpr─Бс╣З─Бс╣Г mat├бyaс╕е,

107.24 v├нpr─Бso mat├нbhiс╕е, X.6.5 v├нpr─Бso mat├нbhiс╕е, X.25.10 mat├нс╣Г v├нprasya, X.64.16 mat├нbhiс╕е тАж v├нpraс╕е, X.123.1 v├нpr─Б mat├нbhiс╕е; cf. also IX.71.3, X.11.6 v├йpate mat─л.

I therefore construe mat─л╠Гn─Б╠Бm with v├нpraс╕е in the published translation, as a loosely descriptive gen. In cd the phrase mithun─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАж adhvary├бvaс╕е is taken by Geldner (fld. by Renou) as referring to the pair (or presumably multiple pairs, given the pl.) of Adhvaryu and Hotar. Although at least I.83.2, which he adduces for this sense, does seem to refer to that pair of two priests, in the dual, I think the pl. here instead refers to rivalrous priests at competing sacrifices, which must be implicit in GeldnerтАЩs rendering, given the pl. They could be pairs of Adhvaryu and Hotar or (more likely in my opinion) just multiple Adhvaryus, each performing in a separate sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not see any signs of unity in this tс╣Ыca. All three vss. contain a participle of тИЪp┼л in passive function, p┼лn─Бn├б- in 37, 38, p┼лy├бm─Бna- in 39, but this is hardly remarkable in the Soma maс╣Зс╕Нala.

Griffith

Singer of true songs, ever-watchful, Soma hath settled in the ladles when they cleanse him.
Him the Adhvaryus, paired and eager, follow, leaders of sacrifice and skilful-handed.

Geldner

Der Wachsame, Beredsame hat die rechten Wege der Gedanken beschritten, sich l├дuternd hat sich Soma in den Camugef├д├Яen gesetzt, den die ergebenen Paare pflegen, die Adhvaryu┬┤s, die handfertigen Wagenfahrer.

Grassmann

Der muntre S├дnger Soma liess sich nieder zur Zeit des Betens flammend in die Sch├╝sseln; Er, den zu Paaren die begier’gen Priester, mit festen H├дnden Wagen lenkend, ehren.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe purified (Soma) approaches (Indra) as the year (approaches) the sun, he fills both heaven and earth (with his radiance), he opens (the darkness with his light); may he, the beloved (Soma), whose beloved (streams) are for (our) preservation, bestow upon us wealth like (wages given) to a labourer.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He, being purified close by, like the Placer of the Sun has filled both world-halves, and he has disclosed them.
He with whose help the winners of dear things (win) dear things, he will extend spoils as if to a victor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The interpr. of this vs. is fairly straightforward, except for the 2nd part of p─Бda a, s┼л╠Бre n├б dh─Б╠Бt─Б. I have treated this simile at length In my Fs. Melchert article, тАЬS┼л╠Бre Duhit├бr’s Brother, the тАШPlacer of the SunтАЩ: Another Example of -e тЖР*-as in Rigvedic Phrasal Sandhi,тАЭ 2010. I will not repeat the disc. here but will summarize the conclusions. The major problem in this simile is what to do with the apparent loc. s┼л╠Бre тАШin the sunтАЩ (to s┼л╠Бra-; or possibly, but less likely, dat. to sv├аr); this has led to some outlandish and unpersuasive interpr. of the phrase. I argue that s┼л╠Бre is actually the old gen. to sv├аr, from *s┼л╠Бraz before voiced dental stop, as in the well-known s┼л╠Бre duhit─Б╠БтАЬdaughter of the sunтАЭ in I.34.5. I start with an archaic formula *s┼л╠Бre dh─Б╠Бt─Б тАЬplacer of the sun,тАЭ with the two words separated here by the simile particle n├б and the true interpr. obscured. The тАЬplacer of the sunтАЭ is most likely Indra, and Soma is being compared to him in his cosmogonic role: filling the two worlds and revealing them.

The word order in the 2nd clause of b, v├н с╣г├б ─Бvaс╕е, is worth noting. Both preverb in tmesis and s├б seek 1st position, and s├б overwhelmingly occupies 1st position, as a glance at Lubotsky shows. Perhaps to maintain s├бтАЩs 1st position tendency, often when a clause has both a preverb and s├б, the preverb will remain in position before the verb (e.g., I.105.4 s├б t├бd d┼лt├│ v├н vocati; also p─Бda d in this vs.: s├б тАж pr├б yaс╣Гsat). But it seems from a rapid survey that when a preverb is in tmesis, it regularly wins 1st position over s├б – e.g., III.59.2 pr├б s├б тАж, VIII.20.16 abh├н с╣г├б … – with WackernagelтАЩs position material imposed betweenтАФe.g., pr├б vaс╕е s├б тАж, VIII.21.10 ─Б╠Бt├║ naс╕е s├б тАж Our brief clause shows this PREV s├б order.

As Oldenberg suggests, in c priy─Б╠Бis governed either directly or indirectly by the 2nd member of the cmpd. priya-s─Б╠Бsaс╕е тАШwinning dear thingsтАЩ: тАЬthose winning dear things (win) dear things.тАЭ The effect is rather like the type gaс╣З─Б╠Бn─Бm gaс╣З├бpati- тАЬtroop lord of troopsтАЭ (II.23.1), though the means are different. As for priya-s─Б╠Бsaс╕е, its stem is given as them. priya-s├б- by Grassmann, and it would have the doubled nom. pl. ending familiar from dev─Б╠Бsaс╕е, etc. However, it seems possible (and in my opinion desirable) to interpr. it as belonging to a root noun -s─Б╠Б-. The rt. noun nom. pl. to -─Б-stems is ordinarily -─Бс╕е, which is identical to the nom. sg. Though several cmpds in -s─Б╠Б- do have this nom. pl. (dhanas─Б╠Бс╕е VIII.3.15, X.65.10; sad─Бs─Б╠Бс╕е IV.16.21, sahasras─Б╠Бс╕е X.64.6), the nom. sg. -s─Б╠Бс╕е is far more common. In a passage like this, where there are no other nom. pl. forms to support the nom. pl. interpr. (as there are in the -s─Б╠Бс╕е nom. pl. passages just cited), doubly marking the nom. pl. would make sense. Scarlatta (585) seems to be leaning in that direction, but doesnтАЩt actually say so.

Parallel to the dative k─Бr├нс╣Зe n├б тАЬas if to a victorтАЭ in the simile, we can assume тАЬto usтАЭ vel sim. in the frame. So Geldner

Griffith

Cleansed near the Sun as ’twere he as Creator hath filled full heaven and earth, and hath disclosed them.
He by whose dear help men gain all their wishes shall yield the precious meed as to a victor.

рд╡рд░реНрдзрд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдХрд▓рд╛рдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдиреЗрди рд╡рд░реНрдзрдпрд┐рддрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдзрдирдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдВрд╡рд░реНрдзрдорд╛рдирдГ рдкрд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реЗрдг рдкреВрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рдореАрдвреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдХрд╛рдорд╛рдирд╛рдВрд╕реЗрдХреНрддрд╛ рд╕рд╕реЛрдордГ рдиреЛрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдВ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рд╖рд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛ рдЕрднреНрдпрд╛рд╡реАрддреН рдЕрднрд┐рд░рдХреНрд╖рддреБ ред рдпреЗрди рд╕реЛрдореЗрди рдкрджрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ рдкрдгрд┐рднрд┐рд░рдкрд╣реГрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧрд╡рд╛рдореНрдкрджрд╛рдирд┐ рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддрдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрд╡рд┐рджрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдЮреНрдЬрд╛рди- рдиреНрддреЛрд╡рд╛ рдиреЛрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореНрдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗ рдЪрд┐рд░рдиреНрддрдирд╛рдГ рдкрд┐рддрд░реЛрдЩреНрдЧрд┐рд░рд╕рдГрдЧрд╛рдГ рдкрд╢реВрдирднрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рдЕрджреНрд░рд┐рдореБрд╖реНрдгрдиреН рд╢рд┐рд▓реЛрдЪреНрдЪрдп- рдореБрд╖реНрдгрдиреН рд╕реЛрдорддреЗрдЬрд╕рд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рд╡реГрддрдВ рд╢рд┐рд▓реЛрдЪреНрдЪрдпрдЩреНрдЧрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдкрд╢реВрдирд╛рд╣рд░рдиреНрдирд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдЙрд╖рд┐рд░рд┐рд╣рдореБрд╖реНрдгрд╛рддрд┐- рд╕рдорд╛рдирдХрд░реНрдорд╛ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдореБрд╖реНрдгрд╛рддреЗрд░реНрд▓рдЩрд┐ рд╡рд░реНрдгрд▓реЛрдкрдГ рее рейреп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay Soma the augmenter (of the gods), self-augmenting, being purified, the showerer (of benefits), protect us by his radiance; through whom our forefathers, tracing the footmarks, cognizant of all things, stole the cattle from the rock.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Stock the cattle from the rock: us. = muс╣г; i.e. ‘stole (ransacked) the rock with regard to (i.e., for) the cattle’

Jamison Brereton

The strengthening strengthener, being purified, Soma the rewarder, helped us with his light,
with which our forefathers, knowing the track, finding the sun, burned the cows out of the rock.

Jamison Brereton Notes

P─Бda a contains another etymological doubling, vardhit─Б╠Бv├бrdhanaс╕е тАЬstrengthening strengthener,тАЭ rather like the doubling of priy├б- in 38c.

Note the allit. in c: тАж p┼л╠Бrve pit├бraс╕е padaj├▒─Б╠Бс╕е.

The expression g─Б╠Б├бdrim uс╣гс╣З├бn тАЬburned the cows out of the rockтАЭ is, to say the least, unusual - and on those grounds disputed. A long tradition, going back to Benfey, emends the text to *muс╣гс╣З├бn тАШstoleтАЩ, with degemination in the sequence ├бdrim (m)uс╣гс╣З├бn. This emendation is accepted by, inter alia, Geldner and Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions ad I.62.2 and Conc.). There is one strong arg. in favor of the change: тИЪmuс╣г тАШstealтАЩ is formulaically embedded in the Vala myth (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 39d and, e.g., I.93.4 y├бd ├бmuс╣гс╣З─лtam тАж paс╣З├нm g─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬwhen you two stole the cows from the niggardтАЭ). Other possible args. are inconclusive: both тИЪmuс╣г and тИЪuс╣г have a 9th class pres., though the latter is only represented by one other form, part. uс╣гс╣З├бn in II.4.7 - but тИЪuс╣г is a poorly attested root. The preverb abh├н found in our passage does not appear with either root. In the end the clinching arg. seems to me to come from Oldenberg, who does not accept the emendation: the meter. The proposed change converts a good cadence into a bad one. Bloomfield (Rig-Veda Repetitions) argues тАЬthat the change from ├бdrim muс╣гс╣З├бn to ├бdrim uс╣гс╣З├бn was made by the redactor in deference to the meter.тАЭ But why would the poet have produced a bad cadence in the first place? I think it more likely that the poet was playing on the rhyming roots тИЪmuс╣г and тИЪuс╣г, with full knowledge that the former is the standard one in the Vala myth, and he is forcing us to invent a new and more difficult image with the latter root. By supplying us with jy├│tiс╣г─Б he is providing us with the means to do so. Oldenberg adduces X.87.12 jy├│tiс╣г─Б тАж ny ├▓с╣гa тАЬwith light burn down тАж,тАЭ comparable to our тАж jy├│tiс╣г─Б / y├йn─Б тАж uс╣гс╣З├бn and with a verb form of тИЪuс╣г.

A poet who could deploy the тАЬplacer of the sunтАЭ formula in the manner he did in the previous vs. is surely capable of such a sly play on words.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not see any signs of unity in this tс╣Ыca. All three vss. contain a participle of тИЪp┼л in passive function, p┼лn─Бn├б- in 37, 38, p┼лy├бm─Бna- in 39, but this is hardly remarkable in the Soma maс╣Зс╕Нala.

He, being cleansed, the Strengthener and Increaser, Soma the Bounteous, helped us with his lustre,
Wherewith our sires of old who knew the footsteps found light and stole the cattle from the mountain.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe ocean, the royal (Soma), genitive rating progeny in the outstretched (firmament, the) supporter of the water traverses the universe; the showerer (of benefits), the brilliant Soma when effused increases abundantly in the elevated woollen filter.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As the sea he has roared at his first expansion, begetting the creatures as king of creation.
The bull in the filter, on the sheepтАЩs back, Soma has grown loftily, the drop being pressed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb v─Бvс╣Ыdhe in d concatenates with vardhit─Б╠Бv├бrdhanaс╕е in 39a.

GeldnerтАЩs tr. of p─Бda a, тАЬDer Ocean hat gebr├╝llt bei seiner ersten Ausbreitung,тАЭ seems to imply (though this is not a necessary interpr. of his tr.) that the samudr├б- is a different entity from Soma himself, and his cited IX.107.23 tv├бс╣Г samudr├бm pratham├│ v├н dh─Бrayaс╕е тАЬYou were [/are] the first to to spread out the seaтАЭ (with both samudr├б- and v├н тИЪdhс╣Ы) certainly depicts them as separate. However, IX.86.29 tv├бс╣Г samudr├│ asi тАж, t├бvem─Б╠Бс╕е p├б├▒ca prad├н┼Ыo v├нdharmaс╣Зi тАЬYou are the sea, тАж; yours are these five regions in your [/their] expansionтАЭ (also with samudr├б- and the -n-stem loc. v├нdharman/-с╣Зi as here) asserts the identity of Soma and the samudr├б-. Since forms of тИЪkrand тАШroarтАЩ in IX (like ├бkr─Бn here) have Soma as their subject (incl. in vss. 13, 18, 28, 32, 33 in this hymn), the identification of Soma and the sea seems assured here.

English translation:

тАЬThe mighty Soma has achieved this mighty (work) that, being the germ of the waters, he has nourished the gods; purified he has given strength to Indra; Indu has genitive rated the light in the sun.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Soma the buffalo performed this great (deed), that [/when] as embryo of the waters he chose the gods.
Purifying himself, he placed strength in Indra. The drop begat the light in the sun. с│У

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬExhilarate V─Бyu for (our) food and wealth, exhilarate Mitra and Varuс╣Зa as soon as you are filtered; exhilarate the company of the Maruts, exhilarate the gods, exhilarate heaven and earth, divine Soma.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Exhilarate V─Бyu for his quest and for our benefit; exhilarate Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, while you are being purified.
Exhilarate the Marutian troop; exhilarate the gods; exhilarate Heaven and Earth, o god Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The infinitival dat. iс╣гс╣н├бye is generally taken to mean тАЬto hasten, for hasteningтАЭ here (Geldner тАЬdass er rasch kommeтАЭ; Renou тАЬafin quтАЩil se h├вteтАЭ; Klein GDGRV I.68 тАЬfor hasteningтАЭ; and cf. EWA s.v. Eс╣в 2 citing GeldnerтАЩs tr. for just this passage). But I am puzzled as to which root тИЪiс╣г the sense тАШhastenтАЩ is supposed to belong to: we have тИЪiс╣г тАШseek, desireтАЩ and тИЪiс╣г тАШsend, set in motionтАЩ. It is to the latter that EWA refers this form (and I assume that the others would also connect the two), but either there has to be a de-valencing of the root (from тАШset in motionтАЩ to тАШbe in motionтАЩ - but there are no forms to this root with intrans. value) or the form has to be covertly passive (тАШto be set in motionтАЩ, hence тАШto moveтАЩ). I think it belongs rather to тИЪiс╣г тАШseek, desireтАЩ and means тАШfor seeking, for the questтАЩ. In my view all 20 exx. of iс╣гс╣н├бye can be united under this rubric. See also comm. ad I.112.1 and VII.92.3. In this particular case V─БyuтАЩs quest is for soma, and upon having received it, he benefits us. So the double dative iс╣гс╣н├бye r─Б╠Бdhase ca is a bit of a zeugma, in that these beneficial datives are for the benefit of different parties, though the satisfaction of the second depends on the success of the first.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFlow you who are straight going, the slayer of the crooked-goer, driving away disease and enemies; mixing your juice with thejuice of the kine (you go to the cups); (you are) Indra’s (friend), we (are) your friends.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself, as the straight smiter of the crooked, thrusting away affliction and insults,
perfecting your milk with the milk of cows. You are (the comrade) of Indra; we are your comrades.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich introduces a note of aggression, but this quickly dissipates. The oppositional pair тАШstraightтАЩ (с╣Ыj├║-) and тАШcrookedтАЩ (vс╣Ыjin├б-) recurs from vs. 18, where, unlike here, it was a morally neutral description of the paths across the sheepтАЩs fleece filter.

I do not understand the doubling of abh├н in p─Бda c, esp. since abh├н seems to add little to this idiom.

43-45 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca has a superficial unity from the (over-)abundance of forms of тИЪp┼л, esp. in the middle vs.: pavasva 43a, 44a, 44b, 44d; p├бvam─Бnaс╕е 44c; pun─Бn├бс╕е 45c (the only form of тИЪp┼л in this vs., and belonging to a different stem). Otherwise there is little to hold it together. The supposed transition between the poets Par─Бsara ┼Ъaktya and Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa happens after vs. 44, but as noted in the published introduction, this change of poets seems unlikely.

Griffith

Flow onward righteous slayer of the wicked, driving away our enemies and sickness,
Blending thy milk with milk which cows afford us. We are thy friends, thou art the Friend of Indra.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬPour forth a fountain of wealth distilling sweet juice, pour upon us male offspring and riches; flow sweet for Indra, O Indu, when purified; and pour riches upon us from the firmament.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Purify yourself into the sweetness of honey, into a wellspring of goods; by purifying yourself bring here to us a hero and a portion.
Sweeten yourself for Indra as you purify yourself, o drop, and by purifying yourself bring here to us wealth from the sea.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the (s)va repetition: m├бdhvaс╕е … pavasva v├бsva … pavasva …

sv├бdasva … pavasva.

As in IX.96.14 (see comm. ad loc.), I take the acc. with pavasva as expressing a transformation of soma into the substance expressed in the acc. This use of pavasva with the acc. contrasts with that of ─Б╠Бpavasv─Б in p─Бdas b and d, where ─Б╠Бadds the sense тАШbring here by purificationтАЩ and the acc. expresses the materials thus obtained.

On s┼л╠Бda- see comm. ad VII.36.3. I argue there that, contra most views, it belongs with the тАШsweetтАЩ words, and in fact that in this passage sv├бdasva тАж p├бvam─Бnaс╕е in c is a virtual gloss (or poetic repair) of s┼л╠Бdam pavasva in a.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca has a superficial unity from the (over-)abundance of forms of тИЪp┼л, esp. in the middle vs.: pavasva 43a, 44a, 44b, 44d; p├бvam─Бnaс╕е 44c; pun─Бn├бс╕е 45c (the only form of тИЪp┼л in this vs., and belonging to a different stem). Otherwise there is little to hold it together. The supposed transition between the poets Par─Бsara ┼Ъaktya and Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa happens after vs. 44, but as noted in the published introduction, this change of poets seems unlikely.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Soma effused in a stream, going like a horse flows powerful like a river down a descent; purified he alights on the wooden abode; Indu mixes with the milk and curds, (mixes) with the water.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Soma, pressed in a stream, driving like a steed, has streamed like a river to the deep, as prizewinner.
He has sat in the wooden womb while being purified. The drop has flowed together with the cows, with the waters. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca has a superficial unity from the (over-)abundance of forms of тИЪp┼л, esp. in the middle vs.: pavasva 43a, 44a, 44b, 44d; p├бvam─Бnaс╕е 44c; pun─Бn├бс╕е 45c (the only form of тИЪp┼л in this vs., and belonging to a different stem). Otherwise there is little to hold it together. The supposed transition between the poets Par─Бsara ┼Ъaktya and Kutsa ─Ас╣Еgirasa happens after vs. 44, but as noted in the published introduction, this change of poets seems unlikely.

Griffith

Strong Soma, pressed, like an impetuous courser, hath flowed in stream as a flood speeding downward.
Cleansed, he hath settled in his wooden dwelling: Indu hath flowed with milk and with the waters.

Gepresst hat Soma sich im Strom ergossen gleich schnellem Renner, wie ins Thal der Fluss rinnt, Gereinigt setzt er in den Sitz von Holz sich, mit Milch und Wasser hat gestr├╢mt der Indu.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe following sagacious Soma flows into the cups, Indra, for you, who long (for him)–all-seeing, car-borne, of adequate vigour, who has been sent forth like the wish of the god-desiring (worshippers).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This very Soma purifies himself for you, o Indra, in the cups, insightful and powerful for you who desire itтАФ
the charioteer having the eye of the sun, whose impetuosity is real, who has been sent surging like the desire of those who seek the gods. с│У

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFlowing with (his) ancient food, enveloping the forms of the earth, covering the house of sacrifice which has a threefold protection, (plural ced) in the waters he advances calling aloud at the oblations like a ministrant priest.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Threefold protection: it protects against cold and rain

Jamison Brereton

He, being purified with age-old vitality, hiding himself in the forms of the daughter (of the Sun [=Dawn]) [=milk],
in the waters clothing himself in shelter providing threefold defense, rasping like a Hotar he drives to the concourses.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda b my interpr. differs significantly from that of Geldner (fld. by Renou) and that favored by Oldenberg, though all of us assume that тАЬdaughterтАЭ is short for тАЬdaughter of the Sun.тАЭ Geldner takes duhit├║с╕е as abl. and assumes an idiom ABL X tir├бс╕е тИЪdh─Б тАЬhide X from тАж,тАЭ an ex. of which he cites from the Kena Up., which seems a distant text from which to harvest a parallel. He takes the v├бrp─Бс╣Гsi as SomaтАЩs own forms, but does not suggest why Soma would want to keep them hidden from the SunтАЩs daughter. I instead take duhit├║с╕е as gen., dependent on v├бrp─Бс╣Гsi, which Oldenberg considers the more natural construal. Since the acc. with medial tir├бс╕е тИЪdh─Б expresses the medium in which the subject hides himself (at least in my view: see comm. ad IX.73.3), in our passage here Soma hides himself тАЬin the forms of the daughter (of the Sun)тАЭ - a designation of milk, since the gleaming white milk is often assimilated to the sun. I see the same idiom in IX.72.3, though more disguised: see extensive comm. there. The reference, of course, is to the mixing of soma with milk.

The following p─Бda provides a different but parallel image of the mixing of soma with water, with the more widespread trope of тАЬclothing himself in.тАЭ The last p─Бda provides a clever multilevel play, as long as r├йbhan is properly interpr. As I have often disc. (incl. ad vs. 8 above), тИЪribh does not mean тАШsingтАЩ as itтАЩs usually glossed, but rather expresses a variety of harsh sounds: rasp, creak, squawk, and crackle. In this p─Бda Soma is compared to a Hotar priest. But the quintessential Hotar is actually the god Agni, the ritual fire - and fires crackle. So the comparison is to the sound of a lively burning fire, but mediated through the priest.

тАЬDivine Soma, who are car-borne, being filtered (at) our (sacrifice), flow quickly into the cups; most sweet-flavoured in the waters, full of delight, offered at the sacrifice, stimulator of all, who like a god are the object of true praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

In contrast to the tс╣Ыcas with faint or no signs of cohesion, this one is over-determined. The verbal lexeme that dominates is abh├н тИЪс╣Ыс╣г: the preverb abh├н opens every one of the 12 p─Бdas, and the impv. arс╣гa/─Б is found in the first p─Бda of every vs. (49a, 50a, 51a). The part. p┼лy├бm─Бnaс╕е ends the first hemistich of each vs. Most of the rest of the material consists of acc. goals of motion. The goals in the first vs. of the tс╣Ыca are gods, in the first half of the 2nd vs. the substances with which Soma will be mixed, and in the rest of the tс╣Ыca those things that we want Soma to provide us. The result is a tс╣Ыca of utmost banality, enlivened by a small play of words in the last p─Бda.

English translation:

тАЬBring us handsome garments, bring us, when you are purified, cows easily milked; bring for our maintenance gratifying gold; divine Soma, bring us horses fit for chariots.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Rush toward your garments that garb well, toward the good-milking cows, while being purified,
toward glittering golden goods, to bring them to us, and toward chariot horses, o god Soma.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner adds тАЬzu gewinnenтАЭ in p─Бdas a and b (also d) with no textual support.

And surely these garments and cows are actually references to the milk mixture, as so often in IX.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In contrast to the tс╣Ыcas with faint or no signs of cohesion, this one is over-determined. The verbal lexeme that dominates is abh├н тИЪс╣Ыс╣г: the preverb abh├н opens every one of the 12 p─Бdas, and the impv. arс╣гa/─Б is found in the first p─Бda of every vs. (49a, 50a, 51a). The part. p┼лy├бm─Бnaс╕е ends the first hemistich of each vs. Most of the rest of the material consists of acc. goals of motion. The goals in the first vs. of the tс╣Ыca are gods, in the first half of the 2nd vs. the substances with which Soma will be mixed, and in the rest of the tс╣Ыca those things that we want Soma to provide us. The result is a tс╣Ыca of utmost banality, enlivened by a small play of words in the last p─Бda.

Pour on us garments that shall clothe us meetly, send, purified, miIch-kine, abundant yielders.
God Soma, send us chariot-drawing horses that they may bring us treasures bright and golden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬBring us celestial treasures, bring us all erthly (treasures) when you are purified; bring us (the ability) whereby we may acquire riches, make our sacred prayer (sweet) as Jamadagni.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Rush toward heavenly goods for us, toward all earthly goods, while being purified,
toward that by which we shall win property, (that is,) toward a seerтАЩs (portion) for us like that of Jamadagni.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner again supplies тАЬzu gewinnenтАЭ in both hemistichs. I once again see no reason to do so. He also takes the rel. cl. of c (y├йna dr├бviс╣Зam a┼Ыn├бv─Бma) as dependent on ─Б╠Бrс╣гey├бm: тАЬum тАж uns den Namen eines R╠ес╣гi zu gewinnen, durch den wir zu Reichtum gelangen k├╢nnen.тАЭ This ignores the parallel abh├нтАЩs of cd and also assumes an embedded rel. cl. (though not all that embedded). Renou takes ─Бrс╣гey├бm as a 2nd obj. of a┼Ыn├бv─Бma: тАЬafin que nous obtenions la richesse, afin lтАЩ├йtat de Proph├иte тАжтАЭ This is somewhat less disruptive than GeldnerтАЩs, but assumes a purpose function for y├йna that has no good precedent, as far as I know. My own interpr. - supplying a gapped acc. тАШthatтАЩ as antecedent for y├йna – seems minimally disruptive and assumes that the insistent structure with abh├н arс╣гa ACC continues in this p─Бda. The same interpr. is found in Hettrich (Hypotaxe, 550-51): тАЬ(fliesse uns das) zu, wodurch wir Reichtum erlangen werden.тАЭ The interpr. of Geldner and Renou also minimize or ignore the only clever part of this tс╣Ыca, which provides a climax of sorts. With the pattern abh├н (тАж) arс╣гa тАЬrush towards тАжтАЭ inescapably established, the poet produces a phonological play on this phrase in the last p─Бda: abhy ─Бrс╣гey├бm, where the acc. goal, beginning ─Бrс╣г-, plays on the impv.

arс╣гa (the play also noted by Geldner, n. 51d). ─Бrс╣гey├б- is found only here in the RV, though it is extremely common in Vedic prose.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In contrast to the tс╣Ыcas with faint or no signs of cohesion, this one is over-determined. The verbal lexeme that dominates is abh├н тИЪс╣Ыс╣г: the preverb abh├н opens every one of the 12 p─Бdas, and the impv. arс╣гa/─Б is found in the first p─Бda of every vs. (49a, 50a, 51a). The part. p┼лy├бm─Бnaс╕е ends the first hemistich of each vs. Most of the rest of the material consists of acc. goals of motion. The goals in the first vs. of the tс╣Ыca are gods, in the first half of the 2nd vs. the substances with which Soma will be mixed, and in the rest of the tс╣Ыca those things that we want Soma to provide us. The result is a tс╣Ыca of utmost banality, enlivened by a small play of words in the last p─Бda.

Griffith

Send to us in a stream celestial riches, send us, when thou art cleansed, what earth containeth,
So that thereby we may acquire possessions and Rsihood in Jamadagni’s manner.

Geldner

Flie├Яe, um uns himmlische G├╝ter, um alle irdischen G├╝ter zu gewinnen, wann du gel├дutert wirst, um gleich Jamadagni uns den Namen eines Rishi zu gewinnen, durch den wir zu Reichtum gelangen k├╢nnen!

Grassmann

O str├╢me uns herbei des Himmels G├╝ter und alle irdischen, o hellentflammter, Wie Dschamadagni str├╢m’ uns S├дngergut her, durch das wir reichen Schatz erlangen m├╢gen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWith this filtered stream pour on us those treasures; do you, Indu, advance to the brown water; at this rite may the sun, rapid as the wind, may (Indra) the object of many sacrifices grant a son to me approaching (the Soma).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Advance to the brown water: m─Бс╣Г┼Ыcatva = manyam─Бn─Бn─Бm c─Бtake, ‘scaring away (?) those who are respectful’;

Badhraс╕е = the illuminator of all or the root of all–the sun

Jamison Brereton

By purifying yourself with this purification bring goods here in this way. O drop, at (the time of) the hiding of the moon [=early morning] run forth into the lake.
The copper-colored (Sun/Fire), sped like the wind, is also there. The very wise one [=Soma?] also gives (to us) the superior man [=Indra?] to make the charge.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The tс╣Ыca begins deceptively straightforwardly, with a call to Soma to purify himself and bring goods. The p─Бda-final v├бs┼лni concatenates with the one ending 51a. Given this acc. with p├бvasva we must assume the idiom ─Б╠Бpavasva тАШbring ACC through your purification.тАЭ The preverb ─Б╠Бmay be concealed in one of the accented final long ─Б╠Б-s in the p─Бda, most likely pav─Б╠Б, which can be pav─Б╠Б+ ─Б╠Б, putting the preverb in the standard position right before the verb, or en─Б╠Б. Or perhaps, if en─Б╠Б is adverbial in the meaning тАШhereтАЩ (so Grassmann, s.v. en─Б╠Б, col. 300; AiG III.524-25), it takes the function of ─Б╠Бin this lexeme. However, I am inclined, with S─Бyaс╣Зa. (see GeldnerтАЩs n. 52a), to take en─Б╠Бas an aberrant neut. pl. with v├бs┼лni - hence тАШthese goodsтАЩ. See AiG III.525, which hesitatingly allows the poss. of neut. pl. elsewhere.

The fun begins with the next p─Бda and with the first word in that p─Бda, m─Бm╠Р┼Ыcatv├й; as was noted above, the word appears, differently accented, in 54b, and these forms are obviously related to m─Бm╠Р┼Ыcat├│с╕е in VII.44.3. In our vss. Geldner and Renou take it as the loc. of a place name, coreferential with loc. s├бrasi: e.g., тАЬdans le lac M─Бс╣Г┼Ыcatva.тАЭ This is certainly the safest choice here, but a place name is essentially excluded for the occurrence of the related word in VII.44.3 - and of course making difficult words into otherwise unattested proper nouns is an interpretational cop-out.

As discussed at length in the comm. to VII.44.3 I return to the old notion that this is a cmpd meaning тАШhiding the moonтАЩ. In all three passages I take it as a temporal designation, originally тАШat dawnтАЩ. This perfectly fits our tс╣Ыca if it depicts the beginning of the early morning soma pressing.

VII.44.3 also contains the word bradhn├б- тАШcopper-coloredтАЩ, found here in p─Бda c. This word can sometimes refer to soma (VIII.4.13, 14; 69.7), sometimes to Agni/fire (III.7.5, X.20.9), but sometimes, it seems, to the sun: I.6.1 and also the occurrence in VII.44.3. In our passage I think it can be all three: the sun, coppery colored at dawn, is appropriate to the early morning time period identified by m─Бm╠Р┼Ыcatv├й, and S┼лrya in X.170.1 is v─Б╠Бtaj┼лta- (like our v─Б╠Бto n├б j┼лt├бс╕е). As we have often seen soma is frequently identified with the sun, and it is often urged to speed along the ritual ground (and see IX.64.16 ├нndavaс╕е тАж j┼лt─Б╠Бс╕е). But what is most often described as v─Б╠Бta-j┼лta- is the fire or its flames. The ritual fire, the soma, and the sun would all necessarily be present at the dawn sacrifice. Both Geldner and Renou take bradhn├бas referring to a horse, which, in my view, distorts their view of the whole vs. and indeed the tс╣Ыca.

In d both Geldner and Renou take the hapax t├бku- as referring to a horse (Renner, coursier), the same one they see as the reference of bradhn├б- in c. Geldner seems to think d involves giving this horse a sort of superior groom (тАЬein t├╝chtiges LenkerтАЭ), with dat. t├бkave the indirect obj. But as was recently noted (ad vs. 49), nс╣Ы╠Б- in the sg. is almost always used of Indra, and I think it is here as well. Soma, by virtue of being consumed by Indra at the sacrifice, brings Indra to the sacrifice and in effect bestows him upon the human worshipers, and he does so for a particular purpose. I take t├бkave as an infinitival dative of purpose: тАШto (make the) charge, to rushтАЩ - Indra in his capacity as our supporter in conflict. Oldenberg considers, but rejects, such an infinitival interpr., in favor of what he considers the simpler indirect obj. with тИЪd─Б.

52-54 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The simplistic repetition of the previous tс╣Ыca contrasts markedly with the contents of this one, which is mind-bogglingly difficult and opaque. Oldenberg pronounces it тАЬgr├╢sstenteils hoffnungslos.тАЭ Thematically it seems to deal with the distribution of wealth in a ritual/martial context, and it also shows signs of lexical cohesion, esp. the hapaxes m─Бm╠Р┼Ыcatv├б- (52b) and m─Б╠Бm╠Р┼Ыcatva- (54b), also v├бs┼лni (52a, 53c), and of varied formulaic repetition: ay─Б╠Бpav─Б╠Бpavasvain─Б╠Б(52a) / en─Б╠Б pavay─Б╠Бpavasva (53a). My interpr. of this tс╣Ыca, in its many obscure details and in its entirety, is very different from the standard ones. In places it pushes the morphology, syntax, and semantics perhaps further than is warranted, and it may seems at times far-fetched. But it has, I think, a richer semantics than the other accounts, and above all it deliberately avoids the refuge taken by others, to make the difficult words into proper nouns.

English translation:

тАЬAnd flow with this filtered stream at the renowned station ofyou who are worthy of renown; (the Soma) the destroyer of enemies has shaken down (for us) sixty thousand treasures for victory as (one shakes) a tree whose fruit is ripe.тАЭ

dakс╣гiс╣З─Бs?].
The challengersтАЩ challenger [=Indra?] will shake off sixty thousand
goods like ripe (fruit) from a tree, for our joy.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The mystery deepens in this vs. The first p─Бda is superficially just a variant of 52a, but it poses several problems. On the one hand pavay─Б╠Бlooks like an instr. sg. to a fem. pav─Б╠Б-, whose more archaic instr. pav─Б╠Бis found in 52a. But the accentuation is wrong: it should be

*pav├бy─Б. AiG III.117 seems to dismiss the accent problem (sim. AiG II.2.247) and simply accept it as an instr., but Oldenberg considers other possibilities, incl. adverbial accent or analogy to ay─Б╠Бin 52a. He rejects LanmanтАЩs sugg. that it represents *pav─Б╠Бy─Б╠Б (from *pav─Б╠Б+ ay─Б╠Б) on metrical grounds (bad break). I have a similar, but different suggestion that avoids the metrical problem: it represents *pav├бy─Б╠Б, namely instr.

*pav├бy─Б (with the correct accent) + ─Б╠Б, the preverb we were seeking also in 52a, which again would put the preverb directly before the verb. The need for ─Б╠Бis less acute here because thereтАЩs no apparent expressed obj. in the p─Бda, but v├бs┼лni can be assumed on the basis of 52a and the 2nd hemistich of this vs. 53c. Moreover, as in 52a I suggest that en─Б╠Бmay be neut. pl. and therefore there is an expressed obj.

The other problem is en─Б╠Б, which also appeared in 52a in a different position.

Here, directly before pavay─Б╠Б, it appears to be an instr., filling the role of ay─Б╠Бin 52a.

But en─Б╠Бshould be m./n., not fem. Though Geldner (n. 53a) convinces himself it is fem.

(and AiG III.524 recognizes at least one possible case of a fem. en─Б╠Б), I think this is unlikely and, as in 52a, suggest that it is a neut. pl. This means that pavay─Б╠Б (/*pav├бy─Б) lacks an instr. demonstr. parallel to ay─Б╠Бin 52a, but this is hardly a problem. Putting all this together, I would thus emend the tr. to тАЬBy purifying yourself with purification bring these (goods) here for us.тАЭ The next p─Бda is syntactically unimpeachable: it consists of a loc. phrase governed by ├бdhi with a gen. dependent on the loc. Moreover, all the words are known and their meanings uncontroversial. The problem is what they refer to when assembled into a phrase. They specify the place (or time) that the self-purification in p─Бda a is to happen: тАЬat the famous ford GEN.тАЭ Given the ritual context, it seems unlikely that a real river ford is meant; instead it must be a metaphorical place or moment in the sacrifice. Most comparable - but unhelpful - is the phrase ─Б╠Бpn─Бnaс╣Г t─лrth├бс╣Г, which I interpr. as тАЬopulent ford,тАЭ found at X.114.7, in a mystical hymn about the sacrifice. I suggest that in our passage it refers to the place/time of the distribution of goods. I further suggest that this refers to the transfer of goods from gods to humans, hence the metaphorical тАЬfordтАЭ for crossing the god/mortal divide. In the next hemistich I suggest that it is Indra who is distributing vast numbers of goods. The gen. ┼Ыrav─Б╠Бyyasya supports this view, since this adj. generally modifies v─Б╠Бja- тАШprizeтАЩ or ray├н- тАШwealthтАЩ (cf., e.g., IX.63.23 ray├нm тАж ┼Ыrav─Б╠Бyyam), as Geldner also points out (n. 53b). Geldner and Renou simply take ┼Ыrav─Б╠Бyyasya as a PN, again simply to dodge the interpretational problem. Though the published translation suggests it might be the place for the distribution of dakс╣гin─Бs, I no longer believe that the passage concerns the dakс╣гiс╣З─Б, since I think this is a reference to IndraтАЩs distribution of goods.

The 2nd hemistich is entirely clear, except for the nom. sg. subject, the hapax naigut├бс╕е. This vс╣Ыddhi deriv. must be interpr. with ref. to its base, nig├║t-, which occurs in the acc. pl. in the next vs., as the designation of overpowered, indeed annihilated, foes; it is also found in X.128.6 (as nom. pl.), where it refers to enemies of some sort who are repulsed and defeated by Agni. Both Geldner and Renou tr. as a PN in our two vss. (though Geldner тАШSchw├дtzer(?)тАЩ in X.128.6). EWA (s.v.) suggests an appealing interpr., as a rt noun cmpd to тИЪgu (his GAV) тАШcall uponтАЩ; with the preverb n├н тАШ*nieder-rufend, schm├дhendтАЩ in a verbal contest. This interpr. seems to be tacitly accepted by Hoffmann (KlSch 447), who tr. it in 54c as тАЬSchm├дherтАЩ; it is also presented by Scarlatta (112-13), though hesitantly - and like Geldner and Renou he tr. it as a PN. By contrast, I find the suggestion quite plausible; I suggest the sense тАШchallengerтАЩ for nig├║t-. In contrast to nig├║t-, its vс╣Ыddhi deriv. in our vs. designates a successful and positively viewed figure, opposed to the nig├║t-s in the next vs. - hence my tr. тАШchallengersтАЩ challengerтАЩ (ScarlattaтАЩs тАШBezwinger der NigutsтАЩ, an interpr. that goes back to S─Бyaс╣Зa. and Ludwig [see GeldnerтАЩs n. 53c]). As in 52d, I take the unnamed referent here to be Indra, though Geldner (n. 53c) suggests Soma. The extravagance of the gifts and the apparent militant nature of naigut├б- seems better suited to Indra, though a militant Soma is not out of the question.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The simplistic repetition of the previous tс╣Ыca contrasts markedly with the contents of this one, which is mind-bogglingly difficult and opaque. Oldenberg pronounces it тАЬgr├╢sstenteils hoffnungslos.тАЭ Thematically it seems to deal with the distribution of wealth in a ritual/martial context, and it also shows signs of lexical cohesion, esp. the hapaxes m─Бm╠Р┼Ыcatv├б- (52b) and m─Б╠Бm╠Р┼Ыcatva- (54b), also v├бs┼лni (52a, 53c), and of varied formulaic repetition: ay─Б╠Бpav─Б╠Бpavasvain─Б╠Б(52a) / en─Б╠Б pavay─Б╠Бpavasva (53a). My interpr. of this tс╣Ыca, in its many obscure details and in its entirety, is very different from the standard ones. In places it pushes the morphology, syntax, and semantics perhaps further than is warranted, and it may seems at times far-fetched. But it has, I think, a richer semantics than the other accounts, and above all it deliberately avoids the refuge taken by others, to make the difficult words into proper nouns.

Griffith

Flow on for us with this purification to the famed ford of thee whose due is glory.
May the Foe-queller shake us down, for triumph, like a tree’s ripe fruit, sixty thousand treasures.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдорд╣рд┐ рдорд╣рддреА рдкреНрд░рднреВрддреЗ рд╡реГрд╖рдирд╛рдо рд╕реБрдкрд╛рдВрд╕реБрд▓реБрдЧрд┐рддрд┐рд╕реБрдкреЛрд▓реБрдХреН рд╡реГрд╖рдирд╛рдордиреА рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдгрдирдордиреЗ рд╢рд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдгрдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдирдордирдВ рдЗрдореЗ рдПрддреЗ рджреНрд╡реЗрдХрд░реНрдордгреА рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╕реЛрдорд╕реНрдп рд╢реВрд╖реЗ рд╕реБрдЦрдХрд░реЗрднрд╡рддрдГ ред рдпреЗрдЪ рдХрд░реНрдордгреА рдорд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪрддреНрд╡реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рдордХреНрд╖реВ рдЪрд░рддреАрддрд┐ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реИрдГрдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрдорд╛рдгреЗрдпреБрджреНрдзреЗ рддрддреНрд╕рд╛рдзреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдпреБ рд╡рд╛ рдЕрдкрд┐рд╡рд╛ рдкреГрд╢рдиреЗ рд╕реНрдкрд░реНрд╢рдирд╕рд╛рдзреНрдпреЗ рдмрд╛рд╣реБрдпреБрджреНрдзреЗ рд╡рдзрддреНрд░реЗ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВрд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдирд╢реАрд▓реЗ рднрд╡рддрдГ рд╕реЛрдпрдВ рдирд┐рдЧреБрддрдГ рдиреАрдЪреИрдГ рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЕрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдкрдпрддреН рддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдорд╕реВрд╖рдкрддреН ред рдЕрд╡рдзреАрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрд┐рдЮреНрдЪ рд╕реНрд░реЗрд╣рдпрддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рджреНрд░рд╡рдпрддреН рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдорд╛рдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд░реВрдиреН ред рдЕрдердкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рдХреГрддрдГ рд╣реЗрд╕реЛрдо рд╕рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЕрдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН рд╢рд╛рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЕрдкрд╛рдЪ рдЕрдкрд╛- рдЧрдордп ред рддрдерд╛ рдЕрдЪрд┐рддрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдЪрдпрдирдордХреБрд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдирд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐рдХрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪ рдЗрддреЛрд╕реНрдорддреНрд╕рдХрд╛рд╢рд╛рддреН рдЕрдкрд╛рдЪ рдЕрдкрдЧрдордп рдЕрдЪрддрд┐рд░реНрдЧрддрд┐рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ рее релрек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese two great acts, the raining (of arrows) and the humiliation (of foes), are the givers of happiness; they are deadly either in a fight on horseback or in a hand to hand fight; he has put the foes to sleep and driven them away; doyou (Soma) drive away the enemies and unbelievers.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In a fight on horseback: m─Бс╣Г┼Ыcatve = a horse, i.e., a battle fought with horses; derived from: makс╣гu carati;

Pс╣Ы┼Ыane = b─Бhuyuddhe, an arm-fight (person nal combat);

Unbelievers: acitaс╕е = those who do not make an agnicayanam (preparation of the sacred fire-plural ce), i.e., infidels

Jamison Brereton Notes

The difficulties do not let up here, esp. in the 1st hemistich. The clearest thing here is the asya, which presumably, because of its lack of accent, must refer to the naigut├бс╕е in 53cd. This same figure is also the subject of the verbs in c.

The first problem is the first word, whose very form is in question. The Pp.

separates m├бh─лm├й into m├бhi and im├й, with the first then a neut. sg.; Grassmann takes it rather as a du. m├бh─л, with ? This is rejected explicitly by Oldenberg on accentual grounds: the standard du. is accented mah─л╠Б. If it is neut. sg., it can modify n─Б╠Бma; if neut. du., v├бdhatre. I prefer the latter, despite the formal problems. Oldenberg, Geldner, and Renou take it as a modifier of n─Б╠Бma.

Let us now turn to vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гan─Б╠Бma, taken as a cmpd by Pp., despite its two accents.

The simple solution here is, as has long been known, to split into two words: vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa n─Б╠Бma, with vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa a neut. agreeing with n─Б╠Бma. I take this as a naming parenthesis тАЬтАШBullтАЩ his name,тАЭ though I recognize that we should probably expect the masc. *vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б in that context (type nalo n─Бma). Perhaps better тАЬтАШBullishтАЩ is his name,тАЭ which more easily accommodates a neut. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa. (Before continuing I will point out that this is most likely a reference to Indra, whose presence I see also in the preceding two vss. - though Soma is possible as well.) A naming parenthesis is not the standard view, which is that тАЬbullish nameтАЭ is one member of a nominal sentence equating the dual entities (whatever they may be - see below) with this name (тАЬthese two Xs are / make upтАЭ [ausmachen] his great bullish nameтАЭ - so Oldenberg, Geldner, and more or less Renou; Scarlatta [112] also follows this interpr. but assumes a du. тАШgreatтАЩ). As that tr. shows, the standard view also has the merit of providing a head noun to the putative neut. m├бhi that opens the p─Бda.

Why then do I put myself in morphological difficulties, rejecting neut. sg.

m├бhi and struggling with neut. vс╣Ы╠Бс╣гa? Because I donтАЩt think that the two entities are equivalent to his name, but rather belong to him and are deployed by him under specific circumstances, as indicated in p─Бda b. I therefore assume a du. m├бh─л, or perhaps correctly accented *mah─л╠Б, which has been redactionally changed after the passage ceased to be understood.

The next question: what are the dual entities. Geldner (fld. by Scarlatta) takes ┼Ы┼лс╣г├й тАж v├бdhatre as a discontinuous dual dvandva: тАЬsein Ungest├╝m und seine Waffe.тАЭ This is clever, but to me unconvincing. Real dual dvandvas with two dual endings that involve material or immaterial entities, rather than gods or at least animate beings, are rare. And this would contain two entities that are not associated with each other textually and do not form a natural semantic class, one of which is an immaterial power, the other a material object. If there is an alternative, we should seek it. And indeed there is: ┼Ы┼лс╣г├й can simply be the modifier of v├бdhatre. There are тАЬtwo forceful weapons of death.тАЭ OldenbergтАЩs тАЬdiese beide ┼Ы┼лс╣г├й v├бdhatre implies this solution, and Renou adopts it as well, though in his n. he claims that ┼Ы┼лс╣г├б- is ordinarily a masc. noun. I think rather the reverse: that it is an adj. even though its head noun is often gapped, esp. when it is the obj. of тИЪс╣Ыc тАШchantтАЩ or similar verbs and refers to a тАЬfortifying / powerful (praise / thought - st├│mam / m├бnma, etc.).тАЭ The adjectival status of ┼Ы┼лс╣г├б- is one more reason not to assume itтАЩs one of a pair in a dual dvandva.

The next question after this: what are these two weapons. I suggest that it is the two fatal activities described in c, both of which are slangy euphemisms: тАШput to sleepтАЩ (sv─Бp├бya-) and тАШsnowтАЩ. The caus. stem sv─Бp├бya- and assoc. redupl. aor.

s├нс╣гvap(a)- are only used in this euphemistic sense of тАШput to deathтАЩ, a sense that is familiar of course in the Engl. equivalent. The parallel stem sneh├бya- is found only here. It is clearly related to the IE words for тАШsnowтАЩ, and, as I discuss in the -├бyabook (91), the hostile / fatal nuance it projects in context can be derived directly from тАШsnowтАЩ; the re-semanticization of the IE root to something like тАШstick togetherтАЩ advocated by a number of scholars (see -├бya-, p. 91 n. 32) is unnecessary. As I point out there, the verb тАШsnowтАЩ is also found in Engl., meaning тАШoverwhelmтАЩ, though (at least decades ago) in a more or less positive sense. The verb sneh├бyat is accented presumably because it opens a new (sub-)clause.

We must now return to p─Бda b, which contains a disjunctive v─Б тАж v─Б construction: m─Б╠Бm╠Р┼Ыcatve v─Б pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыane v─Б. The first term, save for accent, is the same as m─Бm╠Р┼Ыcatv├й in 52b. I confess I have no explanation of the difference in accent and treat the two as identical, as, it seems, do most interpr. - thereтАЩs too much else going on in this tс╣Ыca to focus on this! Since most interpr. take the form in 52b as a name, either of a place or a person (person for Scarlatta for the form in this vs.), pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыane receives the same interpr. Since I take m─Бm╠Р┼Ыcatv├й in 52b as a temporal designation, I want to impose the same analysis on pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыane. The stem pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыana- is a hapax as a masc/neut., but it is at least derivationally related to the fem. pс╣Ы┼Ыan─л╠Б- (3x: I.71.5, X.61.8, 73.2) with diff. accent (see AiG II.2.184, 197), and the adj. pс╣Ы┼Ыan─Бy├║- (1x: I.84.11) is based upon it. The fem. stem is found in difficult passages, two of which (I.71.5, X.61.8) concern the cosmic incest of Heaven with his daughter, which are perhaps cryptic by design. However, all three forms seem to mean something like тАШcaress, caressingтАЩ.

The -y├║-adj. is by contrast in a straightforward passage that aids the interpr. of ours: I.84.11 t─Б╠Бasya pс╣Ы┼Ыan─Бy├║vah, s├│mam ┼Ыr─лс╣Зanti pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыnayaс╕е тАЬ These dappled ones, eager for caresses, prepare the soma for him,тАЭ with the subject dhen├бvaс╕е тАШmilk cowsтАЩ. The theme is the usual one, of the erotic desire of the cows (= milk) for the bull Soma, a theme of course widely represented in IX. I therefore suggest that the loc. pс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыane here as a temporal designation refers to тАЬthe time of caressingтАЭ - that is, to the ritual moment in which Soma unites with the cowsтАЩ milk. Thus, p─Бda b names two key times in the soma sacrifice: the early morning when the sacrifice begins and the moment that the milk is mixed with the soma.

Even if my interpr. of the locc. is correct, why are these ritual times embedded in a vs. that otherwise occupies itself with deadly weapons and hostile encounters. I donтАЩt have a totally satisfactory answer here, but if the subject is Indra, as I have suggested, he may be eliminating rival sacrificers and rival sacrifices that do not conform to the ─Аrya compact - or he may be deriving this strength to do battle from the sacrifice, which is simply represented by two of its temporal stages.

P─Бda d displays pleasing phonological play: c─Б╠Бp─Бm├нtr─Бm╠Р├бp─Бc├нto acet├бс╕е, where the first two sequences are mirror-images of each other: c-─Б-p-─Б vs. a-p-─Б-c.

(Note that the first c is actually borrowed from the end of the last p─Бda.) It is esp.

cleverly designed because of the discontinuous verb ├бpa тАж aca - the impv. aca needing to be extracted from acet├бс╕е (= aca it├бс╕е тАШturn away from hereтАЩ). This acet├бс╕е looks superficially as if it belongs to the stem acet├бs- тАШunperceptiveтАЩ, but it does not.

That sense, and the same privative+тИЪcit, is found instead in the negated rt noun cmpd. ac├нt- in the acc. pl. The p─Бda provides an exceptionally tricky end to a dazzlingly frustrating tс╣Ыca.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The simplistic repetition of the previous tс╣Ыca contrasts markedly with the contents of this one, which is mind-bogglingly difficult and opaque. Oldenberg pronounces it тАЬgr├╢sstenteils hoffnungslos.тАЭ Thematically it seems to deal with the distribution of wealth in a ritual/martial context, and it also shows signs of lexical cohesion, esp. the hapaxes m─Бm╠Р┼Ыcatv├б- (52b) and m─Б╠Бm╠Р┼Ыcatva- (54b), also v├бs┼лni (52a, 53c), and of varied formulaic repetition: ay─Б╠Бpav─Б╠Бpavasvain─Б╠Б(52a) / en─Б╠Б pavay─Б╠Бpavasva (53a). My interpr. of this tс╣Ыca, in its many obscure details and in its entirety, is very different from the standard ones. In places it pushes the morphology, syntax, and semantics perhaps further than is warranted, and it may seems at times far-fetched. But it has, I think, a richer semantics than the other accounts, and above all it deliberately avoids the refuge taken by others, to make the difficult words into proper nouns.

English translation:

тАЬYou reach the three outstretched filters, you hasten to the one (filter) being purified; you are Bhaga, you are the donor of gifts, you Indu are more affluent than the affluent.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Three outstretched filters: the three are the fire, wind and sun; the one is the woollen filter

Jamison Brereton

You converge on the three filters stretched out, but you run along just one while you are being purified.
You are Bhaga, you are the giver of the gift; you are bounteous to the bounteous ones, o drop.

Jamison Brereton Notes

We meet the three filters also in IX.73.8, where their identity is not clear.

Needless to say, L├╝ders (703-4) has a cosmic explanation.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rest of the hymn consists of 4 vss. Oldenberg dithers about whether this consists of an odd vs., 55, followed by a final tс╣Ыca, 56-58 - or a tс╣Ыca 55-57, with a final independent vs. 58. At least to my mind, the latter analysis is clearly superior.

Vs. 58 has the тАЬfeelтАЭ of a hymn-summary vs., with the expression of тАЬourтАЭ wish in ab, and its 2nd half consists of the Kutsa refrain. Nonetheless, there are no clear signs of cohesion in vss. 55-57, though one might point to the filters in both 55 and 56.

Happily none of the vss. presents us with the desperate difficulties of the preceding tс╣Ыca.

Griffith

Thou comest unto three extended filters, and hasteriest through each one as they cleanse thee.
Thou art the giver of the gift, a Bhaga, a Maghavan for liberal lords, O Indu.

English translation:

тАЬThis all-knowing sage Soma, the sovereign of the whole world, flows forth; distilling his drops at the sacrifices, Indu passes through the sheep’s hair on both sides.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This one, knowing all, possessing inspired thoughts, purifies himselfтАФ Soma, the king of all creation.
Rousing the droplets at the rites, the drop proceeds over and across the sheepтАЩs fleece all at once.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the phonological play in d: v├н v─Б╠Бram ├бvyaс╣Г sam├бy─Б╠Бti y─Бti. The last bit is reminiscent of 54d, in that the phonological agreement crosscuts the word divisions: we have rhyming -y─Б╠Бti y─Бti, but the first y─Б╠Бti is to be segmented (sam├б)y─Б ├бti.

55-58 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The rest of the hymn consists of 4 vss. Oldenberg dithers about whether this consists of an odd vs., 55, followed by a final tс╣Ыca, 56-58 - or a tс╣Ыca 55-57, with a final independent vs. 58. At least to my mind, the latter analysis is clearly superior.

Vs. 58 has the тАЬfeelтАЭ of a hymn-summary vs., with the expression of тАЬourтАЭ wish in ab, and its 2nd half consists of the Kutsa refrain. Nonetheless, there are no clear signs of cohesion in vss. 55-57, though one might point to the filters in both 55 and 56.

Happily none of the vss. presents us with the desperate difficulties of the preceding tс╣Ыca.

Griffith

This Soma here, the Wise, the All-obtainer, flows on his way as King of all existence.
Driving the drops at our assemblies, Indu completely traverses the fleecy filter.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe adorable, unassailable (deities) sip the Soma juice, they hail it at its station like worshippers greedy (of wealth); the skilful priests send forth the Soma with their ten fingers, they anoint its body with the fluid of the waters.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The undeceivable buffaloes lick the drop. On his track the poets squawk like birds of prey.
The insightful ones impel him with their ten fingers. They jointly anoint his form with the sap of the waters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The simile in b is one of the best pieces of evidence for my interpr. of тИЪribh as тАШsquawk, creak,тАЩ etc., rather than тАШsingтАЩ. The simile тАЬlike birds of preyтАЭ (n├б gс╣Ы╠Бdhr─Бс╕е) only makes sense if the verb that expresses the sounds of the voices of the poets (kav├бyaс╕е) is not a mellifluous one. Both Geldner and Renou struggle with this. Geldner reduces rebhanti to тАШbecome hearable/knownтАЩ: тАЬтАж werden die Seher lautbar wie die GeierтАЭ (not the first quality one things of for a Geier); Renou simply recasts the simile: тАЬsur sa trace ils psalmodient, comme des po├иtes avides (de gain).тАЭ

55-58 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

The rest of the hymn consists of 4 vss. Oldenberg dithers about whether this consists of an odd vs., 55, followed by a final tс╣Ыca, 56-58 - or a tс╣Ыca 55-57, with a final independent vs. 58. At least to my mind, the latter analysis is clearly superior.

Vs. 58 has the тАЬfeelтАЭ of a hymn-summary vs., with the expression of тАЬourтАЭ wish in ab, and its 2nd half consists of the Kutsa refrain. Nonetheless, there are no clear signs of cohesion in vss. 55-57, though one might point to the filters in both 55 and 56.

Happily none of the vss. presents us with the desperate difficulties of the preceding tс╣Ыca.

Griffith

The Great Inviolate are kissing Indu, and singing in his place like eager sages.
The wise men send him forth with ten swift fingers, and balm his form with essence of the waters.

Geldner

Den Saft lecken unbeirrt die B├╝ffel; auf seinen Spuren werden die Seher lautbar wie die Geier. Ihn treiben die Kundigen mit zehn Fingern zur Eile; sie mischen seine Farbe mit des Wassers Safte.

Grassmann

Den Indu schl├╝rfen unversehrte B├╝ffel, und rauschen dort wie eifervolle S├дnger; Es f├╢rdern durch zehn Finger ihn die Weisen und salben seinen Leib mit Wasserfluten.

Elizarenkova

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rest of the hymn consists of 4 vss. Oldenberg dithers about whether this consists of an odd vs., 55, followed by a final tс╣Ыca, 56-58 - or a tс╣Ыca 55-57, with a final independent vs. 58. At least to my mind, the latter analysis is clearly superior.

Vs. 58 has the тАЬfeelтАЭ of a hymn-summary vs., with the expression of тАЬourтАЭ wish in ab, and its 2nd half consists of the Kutsa refrain. Nonetheless, there are no clear signs of cohesion in vss. 55-57, though one might point to the filters in both 55 and 56.

Happily none of the vss. presents us with the desperate difficulties of the preceding tс╣Ыca.
